des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	from the incision toward the temple to the second incision; scrape all the flesh that is between the two incisions down to the membrane over the bone, then do the same from the middle incision to the other second one, and then pull out this spatula.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	Then insert into the first incision the instrument called the “cultellaire,” which is very sharp on one side, and on the other side is smooth and not sharp, and is shaped as follows:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And place the sharp edge toward the flesh exposed to the tissue, and the smooth edge toward the bone, and insert it until it reaches the middle incision.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And cut all the vessels that descend from the head to the eyes until the incision is continuous to where it opens into the tissue, and then do the same from the middle incision to the outer one; then draw out the blood evenly and press the area to let out the trapped blood; then place in each incision a plug of old cotton, and put on cloths moistened with wine and oil and vinegar, and ensure that no hot swelling occurs there; on the third day, loosen the bandage and administer a large amount of warm water, then treat it with basilicon ointment with rose oil, and other remedies used for treating wounds, until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	of the rheum of the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When an acute cataract occurs frequently in someone, and you see the eyes cloudy and small, the vision weakened, and the eyelids burned; and the eyelashes fall, and there is deep, sharp pain in the head, and the patient sneezes; then know by these symptoms that this matter and this cataract come only from many veins, and the best treatment is this.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And instruct the patient to shave his forehead, then make a large incision down the middle of the forehead, and another an inch wide.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	Begin the incision from the left temple to the right temple, and let the cut reach the bone; keep your hand away from the nerves of the temples that lead to the jaw; and when the bone is exposed, wipe all the blood with a sponge, then separate the two edges of the cut and place old cotton and linen plugs there; then cover with cloths moistened in wine and oil, and guard against hot swelling; when it is removed, it is necessary to rub the bone until flesh begins to grow, then treat it with drying agents that cause flesh to regenerate.
En teil maniere: pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this way: take two parts of wheat flour, and four parts of colophony, and make a plaster from it; and apply it to these wounds to regenerate flesh everywhere.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of blockage of the ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	Everything that falls into the ears is one of four things: either seeds, or insects, or a small stone or similar object like iron; or seeds, like barley, beans, peas; or flowing substances like water, vinegar, and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When a stone or some other object falls into the ear that does not attach or grow in the ear, then put the ear in the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	If you see the stone, apply a little violet oil or sesame oil, then perform an extraction; and make him sneeze by condition, and block his nostrils when the sneeze comes, and place pieces of cloth or wool around the ear; and tilt the ear upwards.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	Many times, it comes out by this treatment; and if it does not come out, perform an extraction with fine pincers, shaped as follows:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it jumps out with the pincers, that’s good; if not, perform an extraction with a fine hook with a small bend; and if it does not jump out with that, then make a small brass tube and put the end of the tube firmly into the ear opening, and stop up what is around the tube with soft wax so that no air can enter along with the tube; then pull it out forcefully, for many times it comes out as we have said; and if it does not come out in this way, then take birdlime, which birds are caught with, and put it on the end of some instrument suitable for this, and wrap a bit of cotton around it; then press the birdlime against the stone or whatever it is, and pull it out.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not come out from all of these treatments that we have said, then hasten to cut the ear before a hot swelling or spasm occurs; and the method of cutting is this: first, bleed the patient from the cephalic vein, and draw blood according to his strength, then make the patient sit between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and make a small cut at the root of the ear at the soft part of the attached place; and let the cut be crescent-shaped, until you reach the stone, then remove it as best you can, and quickly suck it out with your mouth; and treat it until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is a seed that is in there and it swells, then perform an extraction; and if it cannot come out, use a thin, fine spatula as follows:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and make an incision on that seed.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But do not do this when you think that the seed is softened by the moisture of the ear, until you have broken it into pieces; then extract it with fine pincers and by suction, as we have said, so that the extraction is easier.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In the case of water that falls into the ear, the patient should first sneeze by condition, and fill the ear with old cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And let him lie on the same ear in which the water is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If it comes out that way, that’s good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	If not, then take several stones about the length of your finger, thin and light, and warm them a little in the fire; and the patient should put one into the opening of his ear, and jump on one of his feet on the other side, and strike another stone on the one in the ear; and continue to do this from stone to stone until all the water comes out, and thus it will all come out. And if you wish, take a reed, put one end in the ear, and set fire to the other end until most of the reed is burnt; then repeat the same with other reeds until all the water comes out, as we have said with the stone.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	For the extraction of an insect, if it is small-bodied, like a flea or something similar, treat it as we have said in the section; but if it is large enough to feel, then perform extraction with pincers; and it is the easiest thing to remove from the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	For the extraction of worms bred in the ears, when you treat it as we have said in the section and in the chapter on distillations, and the treatment does not work, it is necessary to look at the ear in the sunlight: if you see any worms there, extract them with fine pincers, and if they do not appear, take the tube in the following shape:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And let it be narrow at the bottom and wide at the top.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	And put the finer end into the ear as much as the patient can tolerate, then suck strongly on the whole tube; do this often until all the worms come out.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And if they do not come out, then stop up around the tube with cotton as I said with the stone; and if they do not come out as we have said, then administer distillations that the ancients have tested for killing worms, and you will find them in the chapter on distillations. And then pour your oils and medicines into the ear with this instrument, shaped as you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And let it be silver or brass, narrow at the bottom with a small hole, and open at the top for pouring; and to press the liquid for distillation, use a brass instrument well made for this, and if you wish, take a rasper and wrap some cotton around its tip; then put your oil or juice, and whichever of your medicines you wish, in the tube, and let the tube be in the ear; then insert the rasper with the cotton, and press your hand gently until the oil distills to the bottom of the ear; and the patient will feel it inside, and let the distillation be warmed a bit in the fire before it is poured into the ear; and take care that it is not too cold, for the medicine would not be as good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the blockage of the ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	Some children are born without any opening in the ears; and this same thing happens to men due to blockage from a wound, or flesh growing inside the ear, and this blockage sometimes goes deep within the ear, so that it cannot be seen; and sometimes it occurs a bit outside the opening, and can be seen well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	Thus, that which goes deep, if it cannot be seen, is difficult to cure in many ways, and for that which can be seen, you must place the patient’s ear to the sun; and look inside: if you see the blockage clearly, then treat it with this instrument, whose shape is as follows:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And let it be sharp and cutting at both the front and back in a flat way, so that it does not injure the ear; if the blockage is flesh grown or attached to the ear, then hold it with fine forceps, and cut it lightly, until that flesh is entirely removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the blockage is deep in the ear, then take a fine, light razor and heat it a bit in the fire, then place it on the ear surface.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If you feel a blockage that causes the patient to feel pain while hearing, pierce it lightly, and take care not to injure the nerves of the ear; then place a tent in the ear, according to the width of the opening, and moisten it with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this for several days until the wound is healed, or take a tent and moisten it with rose water, and sprinkle crushed vitriol on it; and if you see the ear swollen, you must remove the tent and replace it with another tent moistened with a wax plaster made of rose oil and wax, until the swelling is removed; then treat it until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if a flow of blood occurs, dip a sponge and cloth in cold water, and place it on the ear, and use other treatments that stop the flow of blood which are in the treatise on distillations.
de la char des papieres	of the flesh of the eyelids
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	These little growths that come on the eyelids when they are moist or dry, you must extend them with tongs and forceps, and cut them from their roots with a small blade; then put crushed vitriol on the spot.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if blood flows, cauterize it with a fine lenticular cautery, and cauterization after incision is effective; and often they reappear when anything remains of their roots; but when they are cauterized by fire, the roots are burned and do not return.
de la gresle	of hail-like lumps
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Often things come on the eyelids that resemble hail in form and hardness, and for this reason, this condition is called “hailstone,” and it is an accumulation of thick moisture on the upper and lower eyelid; the procedure is as follows: observe if the hailstone moves from one side to another, and this is easy to detect; then cut it broadly, peel each part lightly, then take it with forceps and cut it.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	If you cannot cut it without piercing the eyelid a bit, this does not harm the patient; and if the incision is large, close it with stitches and treat it until it is healed; and if it is small, do not stitch it, as the ointment will quickly heal and generate flesh.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the hailstone descends inside the ear toward the upper part, invert the eyelid, extend the hailstone with forceps, cut it, and press from both sides; if the eyelid is pulled away by the incision, this does not harm anything; and when the hailstone is cut, wash the eye with salted water, and treat the spot with a flesh-generating remedy until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	of fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	Exinach is a fat that grows in the membranes of the upper eyelids, and this happens more to children than to anyone else, and it greatly troubles their eyes; they have morning cataracts and cannot look at the sunlight because the tears quickly reach their eyes; therefore, they often lie on their faces and sleep thus, and their eyelids beneath the eyebrows are moist, so that swelling and appearance are covered with exinach, which is visible in the eye.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press the spot with your fingers, you feel the exinach between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the procedure is that the patient should rest their head on your chest; then take a piece of linen, and prepare a tent in the shape of a circle according to the amount of exinach from each part, then place it on the spot; press with your fingers from both sides so that the exinach is gathered in the middle of the circle; then in the center of the moisture make an incision with a sharp blade as wide as the wound made in vein bleeding; and cut deep into the skin until you reach the exinach; and in many cases the exinach emerges from the incision in the shape of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Then remove it with a piece of cloth pressed between your fingers from the outside, and turn your hand to the right and left until it is expelled; and be careful not to insert the blade further, so that you do not go too far with the blade toward the eye and injure it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	If the exinach does not appear at the beginning of the incision, then slightly enlarge the incision lightly until it appears; then remove it as we have described, then moisten cloths in vinegar and water, and apply to the spot, and wrap it with bandages.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And there are some people who grind salt and apply it to spoil any remaining moisture.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat it until it is healed.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if a hot abscess appears at the spot, treat it with soothing plasters until it is healed.
des poilz des papieres	of the hairs of the eyelids
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc IIII manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When additional unnatural hairs grow on the eyelids and are aged, they harm the eyes, causing ailments like frequent tearing, softening of the eyelids, and whitening, eventually leading to eye destruction; the treatment is according to four methods: either by cautery with fire, or by acute medicine as previously in the chapter on cautery, or by incision and stitching, or by caustics, as I will describe.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	You should place the patient’s head on your chest, then turn the eyelid of the eye with your left hand; if it turns easily, that’s good; if not, insert a needle with a thread above it; and place this at the edge of the eyelid where the hairs grow, near those hairs, and pull the thread upwards with the entire eyelid, and turn it toward the razor; then make a cut under the eyelid, beneath the additional hairs, with the cutting spatula, from the large tear duct to the small one; then pull out the thread and place under the eyelid a small tent of cotton and linen, then mark a hooked shape on the eyelid, like a myrtle leaf, and in all cases the figure should match the amount you want to raise the eyelid for everyone.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And if it is necessary to cut a large portion of the eyelid according to how softened the eyelid is; then cut along the two lines you have marked with the spatula, beginning from the large tear duct to the small one; and let one of the incisions be close to the natural hairs in the width of a root, then insert the forceps into one of the two corners of the wound, then peel it all off; then bring together the two lips with a stitch using a needle with a fine wool thread, and wipe off the blood, and burn off the excess threads above the two eyebrows with something sticky, if you wish to do this; if not, you need not bother with it, then leave the stitches and threads in place for three or four days; then treat the wound without stitching with drying and constrictive things, as the eyelid lifts with the closing of the wound and its joining, but stitching is gentler (as the ancients said), and this is done without fear; and there is another method: mark the eyelid with a figure like a myrtle leaf, as we have described, in three separate curves according to the form here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	then cut what extends beyond with small forces evenly according to the form here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And if you do not have the strength to hold the pliers, and the thing is not even, then take a needle with a thread, and insert it into the middle of the area; then place another thread near the large tear duct, and the second thread near the small one, and assemble the threads evenly between your fingers; then lift your hand evenly, and lift up all the skin where you have marked, as we have indicated, then bring together the two edges of the wound by stitching, and treat it until it is healed; and if an abscess appears at your incision, soothe it with cerate and similar softening ointments; and sometimes the hairs of the eyelid are turned inward: then you must follow what we have said about incision; but the stitching in one and the other is more skillful.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The treatment of canthus deformities follows this method: you invert the eyelid and cut it inward as I have said, and then make two small clamps artfully, with two fine ties as long as the eyelid and as wide as the spatumile; then cut at the two heads on both sides where you hold the threads; then subtly bring one and the other together over what extends from the eyelid of the eye, and tighten the two clamps on both sides firmly; and leave it like that for some days, and the skin that is pinched will die, blacken, and decay, until it falls off on its own.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it delays, then cut it with scissors, and then treat it until it is healed; and when the wound is fused, and the eyelid is raised, the hairs will no longer prick; and this is the form of the two clamps you will make according to this shape, and according to this quantity of length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	the procedure is such that you take a fine needle, and insert a thread of soft, fine silk; then gather the ends and tie them subtly, and let the length of the threads be a palm’s length; then insert in the chamber another fine silk thread briefly, and tie the ends of the thread; then place the patient’s head against your chest; and be near the sun so that the procedure is illuminated, for it is a subtle and delicate operation; then insert the needle with the chamber at the root of the adjoining hair, and quickly pierce it into the eyelid so that you pull it above the natural hair; then pull the hair up to the chamber, and place that hair in the chamber, whether there is one, two, three, or more; then pull your hand so that the hairs emerge entirely with the chamber in the eyelid with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the chamber is pulled and the hair does not come out with it, then pull the chamber downward with the thread you have set there, until the chamber comes out of the opening above and you can see it with your eye; then pull out the chamber and the thread, and close the eye and leave it closed for two or three days, until the hair settles in its place and flesh grows over it; and if the hair is short, then attach a long natural hair, and lift it with the one you leave, until it is extended and then remove it.
de la porriture de l’oil	of the decay of the eye
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this illness called "aleacrati," or decay, occurs in the eye, it takes two forms: one natural and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it arises from wound closures, or from incisions or cauterizations, and from similar causes.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the method of treatment for it is that you split that closure, separate its edges, and insert linen tents within, and bind it until it is healed; and it is not appropriate to use drying and contracting substances in its treatment.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	For if you do so, the illness will return worse than the first; instead, work with softening agents, such as fenugreek; and moisten it with water in which mallow and flaxseed have been cooked, and anoint with melted diachylon ointment in one of the oils, and wrap a tent in it, and treat it with this.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasure of your cure is that you take care that it does not close in the same shape it was before; and this procedure we have mentioned serves only as a correction for this illness, so that it does not return in the same shape as before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the flesh that grows in the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This illness that is beneath, which is truly called "axacrati," is both natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	The accidental type comes from wounds, incisions, cauterizations, and similar causes; and the way of proceeding for it is that you take a needle with a doubled thread, and pierce it through the flesh, and make it pass from the left tear duct to the right, so that the thread comes out at both ends of the flesh; then stretch the flesh upward with the needle, and cut it with a broad spatumile.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the shape of the eyelid returns to what is required, that is good; if not, then take a razor and place it in the incision, and turn the eyelid, and make two cuts at the inner side of the eyelid; and let the ends of the two cuts be at the two angles of the incision you have made, and make an angle so that when they are joined, the shape will resemble the shape of the letter called "Greek I"; then remove that flesh, in the quantity such that its edges are sharp underneath, of what follows the eyelid, then bring together the two separated parts, and sew them with wool thread; then treat it with the softening medicines we have mentioned, and with tents, until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the illness comes from an incision, stitching, or cauterization, you must make a cut fully below the hairs of the eyelids, as indicated above; then separate between the two edges with a tent, as I have said; and the work must be done according to the shape of the illness, for it varies greatly in form, and the wise master applies skill with all his power so that he may restore the shape to its natural form; and the patient himself, as required by the work and the instruments, must assume different positions.
dou soudement de la papiere	of the adhesion of the eyelid
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this adhesion occurs in some people such that the upper eyelid is stuck to the white of the eye and cannot move or perform its natural functions, it is necessary then to place the point of a razor under the eyelid, and lift it up; and stretch it with forceps, so that you cut what is attached with a fine spatula, which should not be too sharp nor too cutting, so that the patient cannot suffer the spatula being too sharp or injuring the eye; and let your incision, where you separate that adhesion, be gentle, so that the eyelid returns to its natural shape; and all that adhesion is healed, and at times they apply salted water to the eye, and cleanse it with fresh water, and with collyrium; then place a linen tent between the eyelid and the eye, and apply wool soaked in the white of egg over the eye; and after the third day, use the collyrium and binding substances until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the nail of the eye
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	Know that the "nail" exists in two types: one is fibrous and resembles a hard growth, and another that is not fibrous but looks like frozen white moisture, so that when it is touched with iron and one tries to grasp it with forceps, it cannot be taken; and both forms begin near the large tear duct, and grow little by little until they cover all the sight, all the light, and the movement of the eye.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the method for the incision is that the patient places their head on your lap, then opens their eyes; and you lift the eyelid with your hand, then grasp the "nail" with fine-edged forceps, and stretch it upwards; then take a needle, and place a horsehair, cowhair, or oxhair and a strong thread in it; and slightly bend the tip of the needle and pierce it through the "nail" with the entire needle, and tie the "nail" with a thread and stretch it upwards, and scrape the side of the "nail" with the hair along the side that follows the pupil, and continue with the hair up to the root of the tear duct, then cut the remainder at the root of the tear duct with a fine spatula and small scissors, and leave the natural tissue at the tear duct, so that tears do not commonly flow through the incision; and at times the "nail" extends only to the root and to the thread, as we have said; then one scrapes it with a gentle spatula, the form of which is as follows:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And be careful that the speculum does not touch the fleshy membrane and tear it, and that the pupil is not pierced; after the incision, put a little powdered salt in the eye, and a lotion made from litharge, and leave it until the next day; then treat it with whatever is needed until it is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not firm, and you cannot insert the needle, and the hook cannot enter, often this kind of nail is treated with medicines; and they grow as I have described in the division, and if you wish to cut it, then open the patient’s eye, and take the light, slightly pointed speculum according to this method:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And lift the nail delicately above, and if you see it thinning and the root moving closer, then drop into the eye from your mouth a lotion made from litharge and red lotion and powdered salt, and cover the eye until the next day; then begin the next treatment according to the same method, until it is entirely removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing hinders you in the eye, such as a hot abscess, then leave it, and first treat the hot abscess until it is healed, then resume the work as before, until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of flesh in the tear duct harms the eye greatly, suspend it with the hook, and cut a part of it but not all, so that a flood of tears does not come; then drop into the eye the red lotion made from litharge.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	Of the flesh that grows upon the pupil
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	In the eyes of some men, red flesh sometimes grows and covers the pupil and presses upon the eyelids and turns them outward, appearing like a pomegranate flower; and the method is that the patient lays his head in your lap, then opens his eyes, and you grasp all that flesh with the appropriate hooks, and hold it firmly; then cut the first flesh, and continue cutting with the razor until the end, and be careful not to injure the eye in the operation; and make the incision with the speculum as we have described in the incision of the nail and with the small forceps used to remove the pterygium, as the method shown after this chapter explains; and when the incision is completed and all the flesh removed, fill the eye with powdered salt or drop in red lotion and similar corrosive medicines, and place cotton on the outer eye with egg white, so that it is protected from a hot abscess; and if anything remains, and the hot blood rises up on you, and you fear a hot abscess, then leave the eye and treat the abscess with soothing remedies for hot abscess; then return to your operation until it is healed, and do this when flesh has grown in the eye in this manner.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But in any case you must alleviate the treatment of each weak eye by the natural method; and by the incidental method, with the work of iron; and do not place your hand in any of these operations until you see that the member is able to withstand the operation.
des voines des eulz	Of the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	Pterygia are red veins that cover the eye, impairing vision and continually weakening the eye.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	Thus, it is first necessary to examine whether the eye with the pterygium is strong and has no other ailment besides the pterygium; then draw it back in this manner: instruct the patient to lay his head in your lap, then suspend these veins entirely with the hook according to his guidance, and let the hook be finely double according to this form:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en I cors selonc ceste forme:	And let there be two hooks in a single body, graded in this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then gently hold these veins with the forceps, and wipe away the blood hour after hour, until you see those veins moving away from the eye; and take care not to injure the eye with the points of the speculums, and perform this work at midday before the sun, and be very diligent in your task so that you cut away only those veins; and when you have done this, drop into the eye green and red lotion to destroy what remains of the pterygium.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you are not able to complete everything in that hour, then apply a poultice on the eye made of substances that soothe the pain of the eyes, and leave it there for a few days until the pain is relieved and it is secure from a hot abscess, then resume according to the method given above until it is healed; and this is the shape of the forceps:
de la fistule de l’oil	Of the fistula of the eye
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	Doctors call this “arissati” fistula: when you treat it by cautery and with strong burning medicine according to what I said above, and it is not healed, then the method is to open up over the abscess where it must be, and draw out all the moisture within until the bone is uncovered.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is exposed, and you see the corruption and the blackness, then lift it with the instrument of which the form is given here; it is called “rough head,” and it is made of Indian iron with a round head, and it should be pointed like a file as shown in the present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And place it on the area of the corrupted bone, then turn it between your fingers, and press your hand a little so that you know the corruption is scraped; and do this several times, then apply the area with drying medicines.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the area is healed, and flesh grows there, and the body of the hole is sealed, and it remains thus for 40 days, and it does not reopen nor form an abscess, and no harmful incidents occur, know that it is healed; if not, then there is no other method than to restore the fistula to the hole in the nose according to this form: uncover the bone a second time with iron, and with strong medicines, and when it is uncovered take a drill in this form, with a three-angled iron head, and the shaft should be thinned to the tip as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	then place it on the bone next to the tear duct, and move your hand a little away from the eye, then turn the drill entirely until it pierces the bone and the patient feels it by the air coming out if he holds his hand over his nose; and then treat the area with drying medicines, as I have instructed you, and when flesh grows and the area hardens, the material will go to the nose; so it is easier for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	Of the discharge of the eye
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eye fully opens and there is no obstruction in the nerve nor any reduction, it is necessary to bind the patient; then treat him, apply cups or cupping glasses on the shoulder without drawing blood to suck, then place on the eye a binding made of acacia, aloe, incense, and sarcocolla, and then bind the eye, and cover it with bands and cloths; the method of cloths is that you take very soft cloths, fold each in four, and then place one upon the other according to the quantity needed by the eye; then bind firmly above with a tight band, and repeat the cupping to suck without injuring; then remove the cupping glasses and keep the eye bound day and night, and if the binding loosens, you must tighten it more; then remove the binding after the day and night, and if you see the eye recovering, that is good; if not, then resume the poultice, the cloths, the binding, and the cupping until it is healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	Of the rupture of the uveal membrane
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When ruptures occur in the uveal membrane, then it opens and protrudes from the eyelids like a grain of resin, and it is frightening to behold; then if you wish to cut it, the procedure is that you insert a needle at the root of the lower part up to the upper, then insert another needle with a double thread on the side of the tear duct; pierce it there, and leave the first needle in place; then cut the area of the double thread and tie part of the uvea around it, and tighten it well, then pull out the needle and place on the eye wool soaked in egg white; and leave it until the thread falls with the uvea, then treat the eye with comforting things until the wound is healed; and sometimes the wound is restrained by the uvea on each side with a circle of cloth, until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eye presents a large protrusion, then pierce it with a fine speculum that reaches deeply into the eye, and drain the albuginea moisture and lower the eye, and let it settle immediately; then press it until it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	Of the clouding of the eye
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This illness, called “alcunnati,” is nothing but a clouding that gathers in the eye, appearing as descending water, although it is not water; the method for observing this condition is that you make the patient sit on a suitable, upright seat, then take his head between your hands on both sides, and move him until you see the clouding rise up before your eyes; then it should remain fixed there, and not descend so that the light is clear, and the patient sees things as he used to; and if it does not descend below, know that it is water, and if the descent of the cloud is not arranged as we have described.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Then seat the patient with your hands, then take the fine speculum and make a small incision on the corneal membrane where the conjunctiva continues with the corneal membrane and the cornea, so that the cloud exits; and when it has exited, drop into the eye warm water mixed with honey, or water where fenugreek has been boiled with honey, then treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	Of the waters of the eye
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have here the types of waters in their division, and what is necessary for piercing; so work according to health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	You must make the patient sit between your crossed hands, away from the sunlight, and bind the healthy eye tightly; then place the paper of the eye in your left hand if the eye is left, or in your right hand if the eye is right; then take in your right hand, if the eye is left, the instrument called "almagda," or in your left hand, if the eye is right; then place the tip of the instrument beside the crown to the width of a line on the whiteness of the eye towards the smaller tear duct, then gently push the instrument called "almagda" and turn your hand until it pierces into the whiteness of the eye, and feel that the almagda reaches the empty space; and it is necessary that the measure of the way of the almagda be as deep as the measure of the space from the pupil to the end of the blackness; and that is the crown of the eye; you will see the bone in that paper by the clarity of the corneal tissue, and then place the instrument to where the water is, then express it below one way after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If the water descends immediately, the patient will see in front of him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	Then let it rest a little, and if the water rises again a second time, put pressure with the instrument, and when it is firmly inserted and it does not rise, then withdraw the almagda gently, turning your hand little by little; and then place a little rock salt in the water, and lift the eye from within.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then place on the outside of the eye wads of wool soaked in rose oil and egg white, and bind it with the healthy eye.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	We, and those of our time, place crushed cumin with egg white.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the almagda cannot enter the eye due to its hardness, for there are some men who have very hard eyes, then you must take the instrument called "alberit," of which this is the shape:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	Then pierce only the conjunctive, and do not go too deep, but make a slight opening, then insert the almagda, as we have said; and upon completion of the work, prepare for the patient a fitting bed, where he may sleep on his back in a dark place; and he must be deprived of all movements, and take light foods, and not move his head either to the right or left, and be bound according to his condition until the third day; then release him in that same dark room, and test his sight, and make him see some things, and then rebind him until the seventh day; and it is not necessary that you do this at the time of the treatment or immediately after the incision, but it is necessary that you ease it, because the water rises quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	If warm pustules appear, you should untie the eye before the seventh day, and treat it with something that soothes pustules; and when it is appeased, then uncover the sight and place a small pillow on his face to cover it for a few days, and let him remain always in that dark room.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And then let him leave the house little by little, and return to his affairs; and know that no disciple should interfere in this matter.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And there came to us one who was from Iraq, who told us that in his country they would make a pierced almagda, with which they drew out the water, but I have never seen such a thing in our land, nor have I ever read it in the books of the ancients; and perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the shapes of the forms of the almagda, so that those who do not know them may see them; and let them be properly made of brass:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And let the tips of them be of the same fineness, and the back in three sharp angles.
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh on the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	Sometimes different kinds of flesh grow on the nose, among which there are some that resemble multi-legged scorpions; there are some that have embedded flesh of dark color, and also some that have soft flesh of good color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	In the case of these flesh growths that are soft and not embedded, you must seat the patient in your hands facing the sun; then open their nostrils, throw ointment on this flesh, and pull it out; then cut as much as you can hold with a fine sharp scalpel on one side, until you are sure that all this flesh is removed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if anything remains that cannot be cut, then open it gently with a fine instrument so that nothing remains; and if blood overwhelms you or if there is a hot swelling, treat it as necessary; and if it is a malignant swelling, cauterize it until the blood is stanched and all the flesh is removed, then throw vinegar and water or wine into the nose.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If the nose opens and moisture flows down to the palate, know that it is healed; but if moisture does not flow as it should, know that there is flesh grown on the bone above, which the instrument cannot reach to cut: then you must insert a slightly thick linen thread, knotted in several places, with a space of about one finger between each knot; and the patient should put the end of the thread in one nostril with as much force as possible and pull while breathing through the nose until it comes out in the mouth; children in school often do this, and it is an easy thing for anyone who wants to do it; then hold the end that comes through the nose with one hand, and the other end that comes through the mouth with the other hand, and move one end after the other, passing over the knots on the thread.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Do this until you know that the knots have damaged this flesh, then remove the thread, wipe away the blood, moisten the thread in Egyptian ointment, and put it back in the nose as before; do this for three days or more, until the ointment corrodes all that remains of the flesh; then place a leaden tube in the nose for a few days until it is healed, and if drying medicines are needed, use them; and this is the form of the instrument to purge the head, by which oils and medicines are distilled into the nose.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And it should be made of silver or brass, resembling an open lamp like a tube, and the channel likewise; if you wish, make a closed tube, and let the instrument be full to purge the head; it should have a handle at the end to hold it when heating the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh on the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times a disease appears at the end of the nose called "telul," and it grows and becomes quite large, so that it is visible to look at; therefore you must cut it at the beginning and remove it entirely, then put the cautery or a burning medicine on the spot; if you delay cutting it until it becomes large, check if it is hard, dark in color, or has a poor scent: do not touch it with iron, for it is an ulcerated swelling, for when you cut it sometimes great harm comes to the patient; if the swelling is soft to the touch, not dark in color, and you see it can be cut entirely, empty the patient and cut it without fear, and treat the spot with drying and constricting substances.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the nose is cut and sewn
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Know that when a solution of continuity occurs in one of these delicate cartilages, it is of little use, except in some men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is necessary, then, when this happens to someone, to see if the wound is fresh and still bleeding; then join the two lips with a suture, and treat it until it is healed; and if the lips are already separated on both sides, you must scrape all the parts of their flesh until they bleed, then join the two lips with a suture, tighten it, and sprinkle it with dragon’s blood powder and ground incense; place over the powders a piece of strong plaster or another binding plaster, and leave it until it falls off on its own, then treat it with ointment until it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The method of suturing is that you bring together the separation: either with needles, as we have described in the suturing of the belly; or with thread, as I have made you aware.
des apostemes des levres	of the swellings of the lips
