then wrap the ends of the threads and tie them tightly in two places, so that none of the vessels that nourish them can enter within, so no warm swelling may occur; then apply another tie along the first tie, two fingers’ length away from it, and after these two ties, leave a space in the fascia that is under the heart of the testicles about the size of a finger; and then all the rest according to the roundness that the egg holds; then cut in the part that is under the skin of the testicles, until the blood flows, and it swells, as we have said above; then apply wool moistened with oil, place it on the wounds, and apply the tie we have mentioned.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And sometimes the white fascia we mentioned is cauterized after the incision, out of fear of blood loss.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	For this happens often, and leave the tie in place until it falls off on its own; and if it delays falling, moisten it with warm water and apply what we mentioned until it falls; then treat the wound with further care until it is perfectly healed.
de hernie carnouse	Concerning fleshly hernia
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this rupture I have never seen anyone who dared to treat it with a blade.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the ancients said that it is treated like the rupture that joins to the life, in such a way that you tie the vessels, lightly above and below the cut; then cut in the middle, and treat the abscess of what is working, until the vessels fall; and treat it as we have described, until it is healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	Sometimes a rupture occurs in the groin, as we have said, and the place opens; and no intestines descend into the testicles, and if any descend, it is little, and it soon returns; yet if it remains too long in this state, the wound or fascia grows, until the intestines descend; and this happens due to the stretching of the fascia in the groin, as we have said, because it is stretched, then softened, and the place becomes swollen and opens; and the treatment is by cautery, as we have previously said; and sometimes it is treated by surgery in this manner: the patient should lie often on his back with your support, then cut the place of the swollen rupture in width to the size of three fingers; and then pull out the fascia that is under the skin that follows, then take the wire and place it on the visible area of the fascia; press it down to the depth of the abdomen, then stitch the two visible ends of the fascia on top of the wire, and stitch one and the other; then remove the end of the wire, and do not cut the fascia nor extend the egg or anything else, as I have instructed you in the treatment of intestinal rupture; then treat it according to the treatment of wounds.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you cut the threads, cleanse it and treat the wound until it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The fascia is tightened and does not appear in the rupture, and the cauterization is better in this place and closer to healing.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	On the softening of the skin of the testicles
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a III costures ou IIII fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Often the skin of the testicles softens in some men, because the flesh within is softened, and it is unsightly to see; and when one wants to treat it, make the patient lie on his back, and cut the softened skin over the natural skin; then join the two edges with one stitch, and if you wish, first stitch the excess softened skin with three or four strong stitches; then cut between the stitches, and treat it like other wounds, until it is healed and the threads fall off.
dou chastrement	On castration
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	Know that castration is forbidden in our law, and for this reason I would prefer not to speak of it in this book; and it is only necessary for two reasons: one is so that the physician may know how to respond when asked and know the treatment; and the other, because we often need to castrate certain animals to help us, such as goats, sheep, cats, and other animals.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I say then that castration is done in two ways: either by pulling or by cutting.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In the method done by pulling, make the animal sit in warm water until the testicles are softened and hanging; then take them in your hand until they are released and you no longer feel them.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	For castration by cutting: you must hold the animal, pressing the skin of the testicles with your left hand, then tie the suspensory ligament, and cut each testicle with one cut, once you have skinned them well; leave a little of the fascia and the delicate fascia over the vessels; and this method of castration is better than the pulling method, because in pulling, some part of the testicles might remain, causing the animal to desire mating; then treat the wound until it is healed.
des hermofrodites	On hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	Hermaphroditism appears in two ways in men: one is that between the two testicles appears a form resembling a woman's anatomy, with hair, and sometimes urine flows there.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other type is in women, and above the groin appears a structure like a penis and two testicles.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	And the treatment for both men and women is to cut away all the additional flesh, and treat it as with other wounds; in the second type, in men where urine exits through the skin of the testicles, there is no cure.
de la tentigene	On a tentigene (growth)
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	A tentigene is an added piece of flesh on the natural part, to the point where it is very unsightly; and some women have it as large as a hand, and here is the treatment.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	You must hold the excess of the tentigene with your hand or with hooks and cut it carefully; do not go too deep to avoid bleeding, then treat it with other treatments until it is healed; and there is another flesh that grows at the mouth of the vulva, fills it, and sometimes comes out, resembling a tail, and thus the ancients called it “tail sickness.”
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	You must cut it, as we have said for the tentigene, and treat it until it is healed.
de erratique	On erratic obstruction
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	Erratic obstruction occurs when the woman’s passage is not open or the opening is small; it is caused by birth, or by a disease that has appeared there; or it may be due to added flesh, or thin or thick fascia, and it may lie deep in the womb, on the sides, or beneath, or wherever it may be; and it prevents conception, childbirth, and sometimes menstruation; and its recognition is by examination with a speculum.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the blockage is close and apparent, search for it with your fingers or with the probe.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If it is from a thin fascia and it is close to the two labia, proceed quickly and open it thus: place your two index fingers together, and let the woman lie on her back, her legs spread; then firmly stretch the two labia until the thin fascia is torn and the obstruction is opened; then take wool, moisten it with oil, and place it on the spot, and the woman should lie with her husband every day so that it does not heal over.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	If the fascia is thick and tough, you must cut it with a spatula resembling a myrtle leaf.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the obstruction is from flesh grown there, suspend it with a hook and cut it; and have medicines that stop blood, such as acacia, dragon’s blood, incense, along with egg white; then apply a wide leaden plug so that the wound cannot close over; leave it there for a long time, and insert a linen plug; then treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when flesh grows in the womb, it must be cut in this way, unless it is a gangrenous abscess.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For one should not touch a gangrenous abscess that is in the womb with iron.
des emorroides	About hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins that usually bleed, and when hemorrhoids are old they become fleshy lumps; and we have already discussed their appearance and symptoms, and here I will discuss those that are curable.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and fleshy lumps, when they are deep in the anus and cannot be felt, cannot be cured by iron.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those that are at the opening of the anus and can be felt are those that can be cured.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide;  et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	Thus, you should place the woman in a cool room, then extend the lump with tongs and cut it at its roots, then apply powder with medicines that stop bleeding, such as oak galls, dragon's blood, incense, and similar substances; then place her feet against the wall for an hour, and then place her in cold water;  and if bleeding occurs, have her sit in a decoction of sumac, pomegranate peels, galls, and similar things, then take barley flour, mix it with honey and vinegar, and make a poultice on her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	If this stops it, that is good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If not, apply cupping glasses to her back and breasts without making incisions; then take wool, soak it in plantain juice or dog rose juice with old wine, and apply it to the area.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the swelling subsides, treat the area with ointment until it is healed; and the one called "albathir" is red, with an appearance like a rough lump, which must be cut as I said with the fleshy lumps; then treat it until it is healed.
des apostemes de la marris	About abscesses of the anus
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many types of abscesses occur in the anus, such as chancres, stony abscesses, herpes, warts, fistulas, hemorrhoids, hot abscesses, and many other diseases that I have mentioned in the division.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe;  et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	Thus, I must discuss here the hot abscess that occurs in the anus, which is not one of the abscesses that collects pus;  and if you wish to use an instrument, see if the abscess is acute in its early stages, and full of heat and fever, and if it becomes red if you can see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Then do not hasten to pierce it, but let it mature until the pain subsides; then have the patient sit on a seat, with two small supports to lean on, supported on his back and with his feet positioned outwardly alongside the legs; his thighs should be spread, and his arms placed under his knees, then bound securely with a good tie; then bring his head towards the right side, and administer the instrument used to open the mouth of the anus, of which the form is described hereafter; and it is necessary that when you administer this instrument, you first insert a guide to know the depth of the anus, so that what enters from the instrument does not go deeper than it should and does not harm the patient; and if the instrument is larger, then it is necessary to cover the depth of the anus with cloths so that the instrument does not cause discomfort; and it is necessary to place the end of the instrument above, and to hold the instrument steady.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	And when the abscess opens, and is gently split by hand, it is necessary to cut it at the head with a broad spatula; and when the pus is emptied, it is necessary to place in the wound tents soaked in rose oil or in green, dry oil; and put the tent out of the wound toward the depth of the anus, and place clean wool soaked in water where mallow has been cooked over the anus and the wound; then treat it with appropriate ointment after two days, until it is healed; and sometimes the anus and wound are washed with an enema of water and honey, and then with water where lily roots and long aristolochia have been cooked; then return to the ointment.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is set upon the abdomen, you must avoid treating it with iron, but instead treat it as we have explained in the division.
de l’enfantement	Of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	The midwife must first understand the natural position for childbirth, and the sign of this is when you see the woman bearing down and desiring to inhale fresh air: then the child hastens to come forth; thus you know this birth follows the natural position, with the exit below its head, and the afterbirth along with it; and when you see these signs, you must gently press her abdomen so that the child comes quickly; for when it descends on its head, the afterbirth also exits with it, and the womb is cleansed of impurities through good purification; and any other position is not natural.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For sometimes it comes feet first, or the body or head, and the hands, or it comes upon its abdomen, or sideways, and is sometimes twisted upon its neck, and in other poor positions; thus it is necessary that the midwife be wise and skilled in these things, and avoid error and deception, and I will show you all the positions and how to help in each.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child comes head-first in a natural exit, and the woman labors with difficulty, and her strength is weak, have her sit on a chair, or have women hold her; and moisten her privates with oil or boiled fenugreek, and then the midwife places between her fingers the small spatula in the form shown here:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	and slit the afterbirth, and cut with her nail until the liquid within flows out; and press the woman’s abdomen until the child descends, and if it does not descend, you must give the woman an enema of fenugreek mucilage with sesame oil; then make her sneeze by condition, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour: then the child will come forth.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if both hands come forth, you must gently move them back little by little; and if they cannot go back in, set the woman on a chair and raise her feet high; then knock the chair on the ground, and have someone hold the woman so she does not fall in the movement; and if the hands cannot go back in and the child dies, then cut off the hands with the knife set forth here, and extract the child, restoring everything evenly.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piez	Of the child coming out feet-first
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child comes feet-first, it is necessary to push it up; and then turn it little by little, until it is even; then take one of its feet and extend it little by little.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	When it reaches as far as the thighs, command her to press, and make her sneeze by condition; then it will come forth, God willing.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it does not come out as we have said, then turn it little by little, until it is in the natural position.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it comes out easily.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if it does not come forth as we have said, then take marshmallow mucilage, sesame oil, and melted gum, and grind it all in a mortar; and place this ointment inside and outside the woman’s privates, then make her sit in warm water up to her ribs; and when she is softened below, make a collar of myrrh for her, place it below, and leave it for an hour; then have her sit on a chair, make her sneeze and pinch her mouth and nose, and press her abdomen gently, for the child will now come out.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	Of the child coming out on its knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the child comes in this position, the midwife should place her hands there little by little; then lean it upon its neck, with its feet hanging down, while lying on a bed; and bend its hands little by little, then place the hands upon the abdomen, and remove the cushions from below, so that she is prepared downward; and if the child does not come, take its feet and move it firmly, then move her abdomen upward, then put your hands there; and pull the child little by little; and command the woman to press until the child exits.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	Of the child coming forth sideways with one hand hanging
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	It is necessary to maneuver to bring the hand back: if it cannot be returned, have the woman stand and walk; if she cannot walk, have her lie on a bed, and press her legs strongly; then administer the mucilage I have described; and if she does not give birth, have her sit on a chair, then work to bring the hand back; and pull the child into the natural position, and make her sneeze, and command her to press until the child comes forth.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	Of the child coming out on its neck, with its hands spread and its face turned toward its mother’s back
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	The midwife must hold its hand, then turn it little by little, and pull it gently; and when it is in position, place marshmallow mucilage and oil on her privates, as we have said, then command her to move slightly; and when you have done this, have her sit on a chair, and command her to press; and make her sneeze.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	In this same way, along with the afterbirth
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When it comes forth in this way along with the afterbirth, cut the afterbirth with your nail until the liquid is emptied; and if the child hangs on its face and neck, cut it at the cord so it is not held back and the child does not die; then push the child inside, until you have it positioned as it should be, and command the woman to press a few times: then it will come out easily.
de l’issue des gemelz	Of the birth of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that twins are born often, and sometimes three or four are born; and this is not a strange thing, though it happens rarely.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	Two are unusual, and they rarely survive, if at all; I know that they may be multiplied, and are separated by the membrane that divides them, which is attached to the cord; and sometimes they come out as naturally as a single child, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they come out with difficulty, treat it as we have described, and let the midwife be skilled, and do quickly and lightly what she must; and do this as it may ensure salvation.
de plusors enfans	Of multiple children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	Sometimes there are one or two or three or four or five or six or seven formed in the womb, or several up to fifteen, and all are formed in child shape by the measurement of the wise Creator, and the midwife must know all this, for such a thing may appear to her by chance; and she must act according to what is necessary.
de l’enfant mort	Of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you treat a woman for a dead child in her womb, as I have said in the division, and it does not come forth, and you are forced to work by hand; you must know if the woman is of strong virtue, and has no condition that may cause fear of death; the woman must be laid on her back, her head inclined downward, and her legs raised; and an assistant should hold her on both sides, or she should be tied to the bed so she is not pulled during the descent of the child; then rub the mouth of the womb with moist oils with marshmallow mucilage and fenugreek and linseed; then the midwife should oil her hands with these oils and mucilages; then insert them gently into the womb, then seek a place where to place the hooks that are suitable for this, and observe if the child is positioned to descend by the head; so place the hooks in its eyes or in its neck or in its mouth or on the palate or below the chin or in the shoulder or near the ribs, and if it descends feet first, place the hooks at the wrist and mid-ribs; and it is necessary to hold the hook in the right hand, and put the curve between her fingers of the left hand, and insert it gently with her whole hand, and place the hook in one of these places that we have mentioned, until it reaches the empty part; and this is the form of the hook:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	then place another hook opposite, or a third if needed, so that the extraction is even; and then extend it evenly by moving from one side to the other, to make it come out, and let the hooks be toothed to hold better, as shown here in the form:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if a part remains, let the assistant anoint his fingers with oil, insert them into that part, and pull the other part; if anything remains, apply this ointment to a higher place, and repeat this until it all exits completely.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes before the other, and it cannot be brought back because of tightness, then you should wrap it in a cloth until it fully emerges; then cut it at the joint of the palm or at the elbow, and likewise do the same for the other hand and both feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	And if the child’s head is large and the exit is narrow, or there is fluid accumulated in the head, then you must insert the thorned spatumile between your fingers, split the head, and drain the fluid; or break it with the instrument called the "almidach," which is described along with instruments in the chapter following this one; and likewise proceed if the child has a naturally large head; then pull out the bones with tongs, and if the head jumps out but is held back by force, split it until the fluid in the chest can exit; and if it cannot exit, then cut it into pieces as best you can; and if the child is swollen in the belly or under the ribs, pierce it until the fluid flows.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the child is on its feet, the extraction is easy, and the alignment to the mouth of the womb is straightforward.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	And if it is narrow in the belly or chest, then you must extract it with a cloth wrapped around the hand; and cut the belly or chest until the fluid inside flows; and if the other limbs are removed and the head remains, let the assistant insert his hand deep into the womb and pull it to the mouth of the womb; then apply one or two ointments and pull it out; and if the mouth of the womb is narrowed by an inflamed abscess, avoid working on it; instead, administer moist and fatty substances, apply poultices, and bathe it in softening and moistening water.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if the child is on its side, and you can position it evenly, then administer what we have described for a live child; and if that is not possible, pull it out in pieces, leaving nothing of the placenta.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And once you have done this, administer what we have prescribed for hot abscesses that occur in the womb; and if bleeding occurs, immerse it in astringent water, and administer other treatments.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut I autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman in whose womb a child had died, then another was conceived on top of that one, and the other one also died.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, an abscess appeared on her abdomen, and it swelled until it burst open and began to emit a foul discharge.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to the treatment, and I pondered for a long time, but the wound could not heal.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I applied a strong drawing poultice, and a bone came out, and after a few days, others followed.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was greatly astonished, for the belly has no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	Then I thought these were the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I cleaned the wound and extracted many bones until the woman was in a better state; she lived a long time in this way, with a bit of discharge always coming from the area; and I recorded this chapter only so that, when the practitioner encounters something unusual, he may know how to provide help.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	On restoring the womb to its place.
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	Here follows the form of the press, with which the books are moistened; it has two turners at the two ends of the two bindings.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	However, let the horns be more delicate than the restraining part, and be made of ebony or boxwood; let the mouth of the beam be one finger wide, and the margin of the arms one finger wide, and one and a half palms in length; and between the two bindings there should be two adjustments of the same wood, firmly secured on each side, half a palm long or a bit more; and these two adjustments are inserted into the mouth of the womb to open it when the two horns are turned.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another type, similar in appearance but more delicate and lighter, should be made of ebony or boxwood, resembling tongs; and it should have two adjustments at both ends, as you see, one palm long and two fingers wide; and when you want to open the womb with the instrument, have the woman sit on a bed, her feet hanging down and her legs open, then insert the two adjustments joined together into the womb, and hold the head of the instrument beneath between her thighs; then operate the instrument with your hand as you would with tongs, according to the extent you want to open the mouth of the womb, until the assistant achieves her purpose.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	These instruments are all advanced and their forms are numerous; and when the physician has prepared them, the work proceeds more swiftly and is more esteemed by men because of their effectiveness.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	Do not neglect to prepare the instrument, for its necessity is undeniable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the afterbirth is retained at delivery, instruct the patient to hold her breath, then induce her to sneeze with caution, and press your hands against her mouth and nose; if it comes out this way, it is good.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If not, take a pot and make a hole in the lid, place herbs that can open the mouth of the womb, like calamint, rue, anise, chamomile, cassia wood, and centaury; cook all these herbs, or some of them, in water in the pot over the fire; then place a tube over the hole of the pot, with the other end at the mouth of the womb, and hold it until the vapor enters the womb; then make her sneeze, as we have described.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	Then the afterbirth will come out quickly.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	And if it remains after this treatment and does not come out, instruct the assistant to moisten her left hand with sesame oil or mallow mucilage, then insert it into the vagina and seek the afterbirth; when she has found it, she should grasp it and gradually extend it straight out so that the womb does not descend with the extraction; she should move it gently to the right and left, and then pull; it will come out and detach.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	And if the mouth of the womb is very narrow, we have described the treatment of sneezing and herbal fumigation; if it does not come out with all that we have said, be careful not to force it in pulling; instead, what is at the mouth of the womb should be tied to the woman’s thigh, then apply a tetrapharmaceutical ointment as a clyster; this will soften and loosen it, and it will come out; however, when it decays, it produces a foul smell in the stomach and head, harming the patient.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	Suitable fumigations are therefore required: some of the ancients have tried fumigations of watercress and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The form of the instrument used to fumigate a woman for retained menses or afterbirth is this:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	It is of glass, resembling a tube, and the narrow end is placed in the vagina, with the wide end over the fire; fumigations are applied over coals, and it is held there until it is spent, then another is started.
de percier lou fondement	On piercing the anus.
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born whose anus is not pierced, but rather blocked by a fine membrane: it is therefore necessary for the assistant to pierce that membrane with her finger, and not with a sharp spatumile, and be careful not to touch the rectum; then apply wool soaked in wine and oil, and treat with ointment until it heals.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you fear it might close again, place a lead tube in the opening, leave it for several days, and remove it when the child wants to go to the chamber.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And sometimes this blockage results from the healing of a wound or abscess; then that closure must be cut: treat it as we have described with the lead tube.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula of the fundament
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas that come beneath the fundament are nodes and swellings that come near the outside of the fundament, or in the space between the two parts, sometimes having one or several fistulas; and when that node is old, it opens and emits moist white or thin liquid, and sometimes these fistulas are piercing; they are recognized by what comes out, either discharge or wind when the patient evacuates, and sometimes a worm escapes.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And there are fistulas that pierce up to the bladder and to the middle of the penis; and they reach to the joint of the thigh, and to the base of the tailbone.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And thus one recognizes the fistula that pierces the fundament, or does not pierce it: and this is done by putting your index finger into the fundament and inserting a thin needle of bronze or iron into the fistula when it is not twisted.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if it is twisted, then insert a thin lead probe or a horsehair, until you feel the probe or hair with your finger; and if you do not feel it, and no discharge, air, or worm comes from the opening, as we have said, know that it does not pierce; then proceed quickly to treat it.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula pierces to the bladder or the urine canal, urine escapes from it, and it cannot be sealed by medicines.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it is pierced up to the thigh joint, the probe reaches the place; if there is no twisting and the pain appears around it, then a discharge always flows from it, and neither medicine nor ointment can seal it; and in these piercing fistulas, there is no cure except for labor, and the vanity of foolish doctors who involve themselves in it.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In the one that does not pierce and is not old, there is hope of healing by iron, as I have experienced; the patient lies on their back in your hands, and you lift their legs up to their thighs, and bend the thighs toward their belly; then insert a bronze probe, or lead if there is twisting, until you know where the probe goes.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels it around the fundament, then you should insert your index finger, and if you then feel that the probe has pierced it, and if it is uncovered where you feel the fat or flesh with your finger, then know it is piercing; do not work on it as it cannot be healed.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	It is still said that some can be healed, but this happens rarely; the remedy applied is to heat a fine cautery according to the width of the fistula, as was said before; and insert it fully heated into the fistula until it reaches the fundament; do this two or three times, until you know that this diseased flesh is burned, which resembles a feather; and then treat it with probes moistened in butter, until that flesh comes out, then treat with ointment that regenerates and seals flesh.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If it is healed thus, that is good.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If it cannot otherwise be healed; and if the probe goes in but does not reach the finger in the fundament, and there is a thick cover of flesh or fat between your finger and the probe, and you see the fistula to the extent that it covers the core; then cut it from the beginning of the fistula, and always advance the probe, then the cautery afterward, until it reaches the end of the probe; and the probe will be released, and will fall; then cleanse that diseased flesh that resembles a feather, and let nothing remain of it.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if blood overcomes you, and runs between you and the work, then cauterize it with fire or with sharp medicine.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For the cautery of fire accomplishes two good things: namely, the burning of these added tissues, and the stopping of blood and drying of moisture; then treat with probes moistened in butter or crushed things, until the place expels liquid, and the burned tissue comes out in the liquid; then treat the wound with sealing ointments that generate firm flesh, and the medicines are dry.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, it is healed and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if the fistula goes deep to the fundament and is distant from the body, then insert your finger into the fundament and examine this.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the probe, and between them there is membrane, fat, or flesh, and it is close to piercing, then there is no option but to follow the path of trust and hope, by administering one of three methods: either cauterize it as we have said, cut it down to the bottom, or if you can, place probes and treat as before; and do not go too deep, lest you cut the tissue that holds the fundament, and cause discharge to come out without control; then treat it, as we have said; perhaps it will heal, or you remove that covering and cleanse it once it is cut close to the fundament, either by probe or another pointed instrument; then cleanse that diseased flesh in the wound as much as you can; then take care to restore the wound, and contain the fistula on the side outside the fundament: so it will be easier for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And sometimes there are fistulas in this manner: and it is when you insert the probe into the fistula, and it is on the side of the fundament near the outer skin, then take a probe pierced at the end in this shape:
Et i boute I fil tort en II, et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And insert a thread twisted in two, and insert the probe with the thread into the fistula until it reaches the end.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it is piercing on the inner edge of the fundament, then pull the thread from that hole while you put your finger in the fundament; and pull the end of the thread, and join the two ends together, and tighten one to the other, and leave it for one or two days; and tighten it sometimes, until the thread cuts the flesh between the two, and they fall; then treat the wound until it is sealed and healed.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not pierce, then make it pierce by all the ways that you can, unless it is too deep.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not proper to perform the cutting by ligature so deep, and then treat it, as we have said, until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The form of the spatumile thorn with which one slits the fistula is very sharp on one side and cutting; and on the other side not, so that one does not cut what should not be cut, as you see here:
des emorroydes	of hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Hemorrhoids are in two types: either they are inside the fundament, like grains of grape, and there are small and large ones, and blood often flows from them, and there may be one or more, and they are outside the fundament and at the end of the fundament; but those that are outside have little moisture, and emit frequently or sometimes a small amount of citrine fluid or a bit of blood, and have the color of flesh; and the treatment for those who have them inside the fundament is that you instruct the patient to strain as though to go to the chamber, until the fundament pushes them out, and the roots appear; then act quickly, and hold them with pincers, or hold with your nail, then cut them at their roots; and if the hooks cannot grip them due to their moisture, then take them with a cloth, or with cotton, or a piece of chamelot fabric; and draw them out with your fingers, then cut them, and apply hot powders above that can act as a cautery; or cauterize them as said in the chapter on cauterization, then treat with other remedies until they are healed; and if the fundament cannot push them out, then give the patient a sharp and biting enema to wash out what is in the fundament so it can push out easily; when the patient strains, and the roots come out of the fundament, then the treatment is simple; and it is that you take them with your nail or with pincers, and cut them, then treat as we have said, until they are healed, and he fears the incision by iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	You must administer the suture in this way: take a twisted thread, and put it into a needle, and then pull the thread through and pierce the needle on the other side, and turn the two ends of the thread under the needle, so that it is wide; and tighten the thread firmly, then knot the thread, and pull out the needle, and do the same for all the others, and leave one to drain the excess blood; then place a cloth soaked in rose oil or wax on the fundament, and place it on the fundament, and instruct the patient to rest; and then leave it until they fall off, and when they have fallen, then treat with ointment and other care until it is healed.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	Of the drying of dung in the fundament
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times, drying of dung occurs in the intestine, due to a natural constriction, and when the illness is old and medicine is of no use.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then you must scrape at it with the point of a spatula or with your nail, at the top, so it does not moisten; then treat it until it is softened as necessary; and if it cannot be softened, scrape it again harder than before, until it bleeds a lot and is skinned; then treat it until it is healed.
dou fremit	Of shivering
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	Formice is a small fraudulent appearance around the body, and it goes very deep; and sometimes cold finds it, and it is felt as if a shivering death, and it comes into the whole body, and more to the hands than elsewhere.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the cure is that you take the quill of a goose feather, or a strong vulture feather, and place that quill on the shivering, so that the circle completely surrounds the shivering; then turn your hand with the quill until you cut all around the shivering, and push it in deeply, and extract the shivering from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you wish, do this with a quill of brass or iron according to this form, and be subtle below and draw above:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	not pierced, to better hold in the finger, and better press. And if you wish, cauterize the shivering, as is explained before in the chapter on cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	Of the form of the clyster
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Sometimes one makes a clyster of silver or brass, or of melted or hammered brass; and sometimes these instruments are made small and large, according to those to whom they are administered.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Thus, those that one administers for the treatment of children, and for those who are weak and in pain, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The shape of the small and large clyster is wide above, where the belly is tied in this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and there is a division where the belly is tied, as you see, and the bottom is pierced inside; and on one side there are two holes, and on the other, one; and the belly, where the medicines are placed, is made from an animal bladder or parchment, and is pierced all around with small holes, with a finger’s width of space between each hole; then put in each of these holes a strong thread of raw, twisted thread around an X or twisted around, and tie the belly as one ties a goat; and when the medicine is inside, tie it to the instrument in front with a strong thread, then administer the clyster; and this is the shape of the circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And let the medicine be neither too hot nor too cold, and anoint the head of the clyster with oil or egg white, or something similar, then gently insert it; then the administrator squeezes it with both hands together until it is completely empty, then removes the clyster, and raises the patient’s legs against the wall, and if the medicine wants to escape, hold it in as long as possible; and if he sleeps through the night with it, it is of even greater help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you administer the clyster in a case of intestinal flow, and the medicine hastens to exit, administer it again until it is healed.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if hemorrhoids are in the fundament, or an abscess, let the clyster be as small as for a child; and this is the shape of the delicate clyster on which the skin is drawn tight:
des plaies	Of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already discussed in the division the treatment of wounds; now we will speak of treatments of hands and medicines, according to the fulfillment.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to what causes them, according to the places where the wounds occur, and by what they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things by which wounds are made are by a blow of a stone, and by the cutting of a sword and a knife, or a lance, or wood or a projectile, or similar things; or they are made according to the places of the body, such as a wound that falls on the neck, or on the head, or the chest, or the belly, or the liver, and similar members; and I will tell you the treatment of each wound, and I will begin with simple head wounds, for the memory will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head, and the bone is not broken, take care if it is from a blow by a stone or similar things, and the skin is still torn and the wound is large, and you suspect the onset of a hot abscess: then immediately bleed from the cephalic vein, especially if little blood comes from the wound, and let the bleeding be on the opposite side from the injured part; and prevent the patient from taking in wine or heavy foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he does not want to bleed, let his food be reduced, and let him not drink wine or eat meat; and place on the wound, if a hot abscess appears there, cotton soaked in rose oil only, or in a styptic wine; and if there is no hot abscess, apply on the wound, if it is fresh with blood, and it is not altered by the air, powder, which I will mention a bit later; and if the burn has altered it, apply some ointments, until it is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large, as if from a sword cut and similar, and the edges cannot be joined with bandages, then join them by sewing, as I will describe for wounds of the belly, concerning stitching.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is stripped of flesh down to the bone, and hangs, and only barely holds, then cut it; then treat the wound with medicine, and restore hard flesh in place of skin, and advise the patient to eat heavy foods, such as heads and cooked wheat, as well as chicken, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find rot in the skin, and it does not reach the bone, then cut away all the rot and discard it, then treat it; and if there is an artery in the wound or a vein, from which blood flows, and it cannot be stopped with medicines, then seek the artery, and if you find it loose, then tie it with a thread; and if that does not help, then cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the treatment is light: it is that you place inside this powder, which seals before the burn has altered it.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the manner of the powder is this: take one part incense; two parts dragon’s blood; three parts quicklime, and powder it finely, and fill the wound, and compress it strongly, so that it is well dried and binds with its own blood; and then bind it well, and leave it without unbinding, unless it swells; for the medicine is not removed until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And sometimes this is done with quicklime alone, when one has no incense or dragon’s blood, provided the burn has not altered the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the burn has altered the wound, especially in summer, then do not apply this powder; but place on some digesting ointments, or a poultice of barley flour made with water and honey, until it discharges pus; then treat it with other cures until it is healed.
