Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if a bone fracture comes with the wound, and it is small, extract it with delicate pincers; and I will speak to you later about fractures of the head.
de la plaie dou col	Of the wound to the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If a wound comes to the neck and it is simple, there is no difference between it and that of the head, except if the nerve of the neck or the artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is the nerve, there is no other device than to leave the cure alone, and not to apply anything restraining, for it harms the nerves and makes them contract; and apply nothing cold to the wound, for the nature of nerves is cold, and their continuity is with the brain, which is the highest of members; but let the medicine be soft, such as warm cloths washed in fresh water, and mixed with rose oil, and madder root also washed in fresh water, and other mineral stones according to this manner, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, sew it and bind it with bandages, then treat it until it is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are deep and it is pierced and full of pus, then puncture it at the lowest point; and if the artery is cut and blood flow comes from it, then separate it, tie it, and cauterize if necessary; and if the spine of the throat or the gullet is cut, and the passage by which food travels is preserved, then sew the gullet onto the side of the throat, but do not touch the throat, and place it back according to its natural form; then gently tighten it, and leave it for a few days, then treat it with drying ointments until it is healed; and if the wound has made an impression in the bone, then search for it; and if there are bone fragments, then extract all of them if you can, and those you cannot remove, leave until the wound rots and the passage is cleared and eased; and if the wound is fresh, then apply the powder I have mentioned.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and there is a fistula, treat it as I have explained in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	Of the wound by lance or knife
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is a blow by lance or knife, and the wound is deep, then check if air escapes from the wound when the patient breathes: know then that the wound is mortal; and if it is not deep and it is fresh with blood, do not immediately put powder on it or bandage it at first, so that the blood does not sink deep and return to the heart and kill the patient; but apply an attractive ointment, and bind it twice a day; and if you do not have ointment, place old cotton in the wound to draw out the moisture, and have the patient sleep on the wound for three or four days, or longer; then there will be no spasm, nor trembling of the heart or difficulty in breathing; and when you see good signs, know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Then treat it with tents and other remedies until it is healed; and if it cannot heal and discharges, know that there is a fistula; treat it as one should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is from a sword or knife cut, and it is simple, on the chest or on the back, treat it as described above; if it is large, use sutures; if it is small, apply powder, and if it has pressed into the bone and broken off pieces, examine the wound and remove the fragments if they are loose; and if they are not loose, allow the wound to fester, which will make extraction easier; and for other wounds on other limbs, the judgment is as we have described.
dou derrompement dou ventre	Of the rupture of the abdomen
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	The rupture of the abdomen can be large, moderate, or small; in the case of a large wound, the intestines or the nerves of the intestines sometimes protrude, affecting their reintegration, and suturing is more difficult; sometimes a small wound is worse than a large one, because it is harder to replace the intestines unless they are reinserted gradually; for the intestines swell as soon as they feel the cold, making reinsertion more difficult, and for this reason a moderate wound is often preferable, as the intestines can be repositioned more easily than in the other two cases. And know that abdominal ruptures are of four types: the two common sutures occur in the abdominal suturing, and the suturing of other wounds of the body, and the other two specific sutures are common to other wounds; however, they are more specific to the abdominal suture, and I will explain each one and clarify them.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small, and a part of the intestine comes out, and it is difficult to put it back, it is for one of two reasons: either because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestine is swollen due to cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, warm it in this manner: soak a sponge or a soft cloth in lukewarm water, or cook hyssop, cypress, and spike in water, and moisten the intestine until the swelling is removed; and sometimes do this with astringent wine, which is better than water alone for reducing swelling.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling subside, moisten the intestine with water or with mallow and althea cooked, for this slightly eases the entry; and if it cannot enter, make a small cut in the wound with the instrument used for cutting hemorrhoids; and the first treatment is better than the incision, for one should not cut unless there is great necessity; and this is the instrument for cutting: it cuts inwardly along the curve and not outwardly, and here is its shape:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestine comes out, put it back in its natural shape, in its proper place, if you are able, for it is of much benefit.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is large, and it is in the lower part of the belly, make the patient lie on his back, with his legs higher than his head; and if it is in the lower part of the belly, place the head and chest higher than the lower parts, and likewise, if the rupture of the belly is on one of the two sides, be attentive that the wounded part is higher than the other; and thus it is necessary to apply what I say to large and moderate wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	For small wounds, use what is prepared, then have a gentle assistant who holds the entire rupture with his hand and brings the edges together; and this is the common way of suturing: you take one or more needles, depending on the width of the wound, then leave a finger’s width from the edge of the wound, and insert a needle with a strong, durable thread; pierce both sides of the skin along with both sides of the underlying membrane called the siphac, which lies under the skin, so that you pierce through to that side, and join the two sides of the siphac, all four together; then tighten with a doubled thread around the needle on both sides, then carefully join the two edges of the wound, then leave a finger’s width and insert another needle; then tie the thread as you did for the first needle, and continue as needed with the needles until the entire wound is closed; and the needles should be medium-sized, neither too fine nor too thick, because fine needles cut through all the flesh, and overly thick ones cannot easily enter: therefore, they should be medium; and the needles should not be pushed too far from the flesh and skin, lest they cut and open the wound before it heals; and then cut the ends of the needles, so they do not hurt the patient while sleeping, and place tent plugs or cloths at the ends of the needles to hold them firmly, and leave them until the wound is healed; and this method of suturing with needles is more suitable for small wounds, as one or two needles are enough. The second type of suture is common, where you join the two sides of the skin and the two sides of the siphac together with a needle that has a strong, medium thread; and when you have pierced these four parts together, bring the needle back to the point where you began, as one sews cloth; and leave a gap between each stitch about the width of a smaller finger; people know this suture, and I sewed a wound a man had on his abdomen, inflicted by a knife, and the wound was larger than a palm-width, with about two palm-widths of intestine protruding, and the wound was in the middle of the abdomen.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I returned the intestine after it had been outside for twenty-four hours, and the wound was healed within fifteen days, and I treated him, and he was cured.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And the doctors had judged that he would die, and it was a miracle; and I did not treat him with ointment, for I was in a place where there were none, nor any medicines; instead, I simply placed old cotton on the wound twice a day, and washed it with honeyed water until he was healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Now I will tell you the two specific methods of suturing: take the needle, and insert it from the outer side to the inner one; when it has pierced straight through the core, leave the end of the siphac on the side where you inserted the needle, and make it pierce through from the inner side to the outer; and the idea of this suture is that you sew as furriers sew hides, and that you leave the siphac once on one side, then pick it up on the other, until the suture is entirely completed.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second method of suturing, which Galen aptly describes, is as some do it: they join the two parts together naturally and align one end of the siphac to the other end, in this way: insert a needle at the nearest end of the edge, piercing only that spot, leaving the two ends of the siphac; then turn the needle, and pierce from the outer part to the inner one, at the two ends of the siphac; then pierce both from the outer part to the inner one, in two other ends of the edge that are on the opposite side; and this is the better and more common method of suturing.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galen says this, and others confirm it, that one should sew the abdomen with two needles, with thread on each; and one should insert one needle on one side and the other on the other, in the manner of those who sew straps; and know that when the rupture is in the middle of the abdomen, the suturing is more difficult than in other places on the abdomen.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The assessment of the wound is similar to the assessment of other wounds: if you find the wound fresh, with all its blood, before the scab has changed it, then replace the intestine and sew it; then apply powder that regenerates flesh, and if the scab has changed it, apply any available ointment until the wound swells; and allow the threads to fall out, and let the siphac and the edge heal; then treat the wound as with others until it is healed; and if you have no medicines, then as soon as it begins to discharge pus, apply old cotton, and change it twice daily until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	For you have no need of other medicines in many situations when the wounds are simple; and if you fear that the wound might spread to the principal organs, you should moisten light wool in tempered warm oil or rose oil, and place it around the groin and under the armpits; and if there is pain or putrefaction in the intestines, which often happens, give an enema with lukewarm dark wine, especially if the putrefaction reaches the intestine; and pierce it within, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestine that is called "jejunum" cannot heal when it is wounded, due to the density of the veins that are there, and because of the delicacy of the entire body, and its proximity to the nature of the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the mesentery protrudes from the wound, put it back as with the intestine, while it is fresh; and if it is old and has turned green or black, you should tie the spot that is black so that blood flow does not reach it, for there are veins and arteries; then cut what is between the bindings, and leave the two ends hanging from the part below the wound to the outside, to ease extraction when the mesentery falls, and the wound swells.
de la routure dou boueil	Of the rupture of the bowel
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestine is round, and the wound is small, it can sometimes be restored in some men, as I saw when a man was wounded in the abdomen by a lance; and the wound was to the right of the stomach, and it became chronic and turned into a fistula, and excrement and gas were coming out of it; I applied treatment as best as I could, and did not cease from making fine adjustments until he was healed, and the place was closed.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw it close, I feared that the patient might have pain in his abdomen; but he had no pain, and remained in a better state, eating and drinking; and some practitioners said that when there is a small wound in the intestine, it should be tied in this way: take clamps with large heads, then bring the lips of the wound together, and when the clamp has its jaws open, place it on the two lips, so that it closes tightly; then cut off the head, and it holds so that it cannot come undone, then place another clamp after it in the same way as before, until the wound is completely covered; and sew the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	These ends then burn in the intestine, and no harm comes to the patient, and one can tie the intestine with a thin thread made from the intestine of an animal, in this way: take the end of this intestinal thread, well stripped of flesh, and then tie a thin twisted linen thread to the end, then put the thread in the needle, and sew the intestine, and return it to the rupture; and this method of sewing with clamps is nothing other than a way of trust and hope; and if the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the thin intestines, there is no skill or healing possible, except by subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	Of fistula, wherever it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know that any wound or abscess, when it becomes old, is universally called “fistula,” especially when it is hollow and produces pus.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And a fistula is in truth a hardened false swelling, white and without pain, and it is hollow like the quill of a bird’s feather; sometimes it produces a clear discharge, sometimes thick; sometimes little, sometimes a lot; and I have already spoken in the section on wounds, that any wound which is not healed, and has no flesh, is due only to one of nine causes: namely, due to a lack of blood or bodily substance; or due to its malignancy; or because there is hard flesh within it and on its edges, which prevents flesh from growing; or there is too much discharge; or the place is decayed, and the material is of poor quality; or the medicine used is not suitable for the treatment; or because the corruption is of a pestilential type; or due to the properties of the region, where digestion is slow, healing is delayed, and it swells by nature; or there are veins or bone: and I have already explained all these causes, their signs, and the medicinal treatments in the section on wounds.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Now I must inform you of the treatment of a fistula performed by manual intervention.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	Know that a fistula can occur in all parts of the body; for there are fistulas that appear on the large veins, on the arteries, on the nerves, on the peritoneum, on the intestine, on the bladder, on some of the ribs, on the spine, or on any joint of the hands or feet; and there are some that occur in the primary organ and in similar places.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And all fistulas of this kind are difficult to heal, involving only labor and lack of knowledge; and if there is any fistula that does not extend to the areas I have mentioned, and you have confidence in the treatment and wish to examine it, take a probe of bronze or iron if the fistula is straight, and seek it out; if the fistula is twisted, probe it with a delicate lead probe, as lead bends well around curves; and if the fistula has multiple openings and you cannot properly examine it with probes, cleanse it with a clyster through one of the openings, as the moisture will flow from one opening to another and clean it; then examine it carefully as best you can to determine if there is bone or nerve, and if it is hollow in depth, ask the patient about the pain they feel when you press with your hand, and where they feel it; and once you truly understand where it is, and if it is far from a joint, or from a nerve, or from an artery, or from a vein, or in any of the places I have described, then cut it as I have explained, and remove from within the hardened matter and corrupted flesh; then treat it until it is healed, and if the fistula is very deep in a straight area, you must cut as deep as you can, then place tents soaked in sharp medicine, and push them to the end of the fistula so the medicine will erode the excess matter remaining at the base; and then apply ointments that generate healthy flesh until it is healed; and if it does not heal from this, cauterize it as we have discussed, and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, remove it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If the veins or nerves do not hurt you or the principal limbs, as we have said; and if the bone is exposed, and there is corruption and blackness, scrape it until all the corruption is removed, then treat it with things that grow flesh until it is healed; and if it is not healed, and gives pus as before, know that you have not gone to the bottom: then uncover and search until you reach the bottom, and remove all the corruption, then restore the place; and if it is thus healed, that is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If not, know that the corruption is too deep for you to reach it; then there is no other trick but to leave it to nature; and if there is a small corrupted bone, and you can pull it with pincers, extract it with a suitable instrument, and if there are several bones, remove them all, do not leave a single one; and if the moisture troubles you, and there is no error or fear, then cut the moisture and flesh, and free the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if you cannot remove them all at once, then place on the wound something that induces rot, and leave it until the place around the bones has rotted, and then the bones will come away more easily; and if it is a large bone, such as in the leg or thigh, scrape only the corruption until all the blackness is removed, then restore the wound; and if there is a large part of it corrupted, and it reaches the marrow of the bone, then it must be cut and sliced all the way to the corruption, and then treat it until it is healed; and I will tell you about a fistula that a man had on his leg, so that you may take example and aid in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	There was a young man around 30 years old, who had pain in his leg from a condition that came from within the body, so that the humors came to the leg, and it swelled with a large abscess, and there was no external cause to open it; but the doctors in their folly worked on it until the abscess opened, and much matter drained from it, and it became a fistula, and many holes formed, all discharging pus and moisture from the body; and many doctors treated it for about two years, and there was no one skilled in the art of hands, until I was called, and I saw his leg and the medicines they used to treat it, and what flowed through the holes in great quantity; and the young man’s body turned red, and his color became yellow.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I inserted a probe into one of these holes, and then examined all the holes, and found that one connected to the other from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	So I hastened, and cut into one of the holes until I exposed part of the bone, and I found it corrupted and pierced, and the corruption reached the inner bone; I scraped away what I could see of the corrupted bone, and thought there was no other corruption, other than what I removed; and I began to restore the wound with soothing medicines for a long time, but it could not heal; then I began again, and exposed the bone as before, and found the corruption continued in the bone, and I scraped it and removed it, and made efforts to close the place; but I could not until I cut around a palm’s breadth of the bone, and pulled it out completely along with the marrow, then treated it with medicines; and it was healed and closed quickly, and there was no need to begin the work again except for the weakness of the patient, who could not endure, and for my fear of his death.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For due to the drainage he often bled, but he was completely healed, and in place of the bone a hard flesh grew, and it was of good quality and did not hinder him or cause him harm in any way, neither in walking nor in coming and going.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, it must be scraped in this way: take a bandage, and tie it to the end of the bone that is exposed, and order someone to pull it upwards; and put another woolen bandage, thicker than the first, and tie it over the flesh that is over the bone, and extend the end, so that you draw the corrupted flesh below, and expose the flesh over the place where you want to scrape, so that the scraping does not injure the flesh; and place a stick or a board under the bone to protect the corrupted flesh; and it is necessary to scrape as long as one can see and feel the corruption, and to scrape again another time.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	And if the bone is corrupted and not at all visible, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part of it, then expose all the flesh; then place a hot iron below, and then pass a saw from one end of the corruption to the other, and let the sawing be a little longer than the length of the corruption, as we have said; and if the corruption is in the joint, then cut the corrupted joint and saw the bone on the side where it connects to the other part; and if the corruption is in the connection between two joints, then there is no other solution than cutting; and if the corruption is in the wrist of the hand or the ankle of the foot, this is a very serious matter, yet it is necessary that you examine this corrosion, in whatever way it becomes apparent to you; and cleanse it in every way that you can, provided that neither the veins nor the nerves work against you; and know that the saws and the instruments for cutting these bones are numerous, according to the position of the bones, their appearance, their thickness and their thinness, their size and their smallness, and their hardness; and therefore, it is necessary to prepare an instrument adapted to each specific situation; and know that the work will indicate to you the instrument you need, in accordance with the knowledge of this art and the testimony of the various types of diseases; so consider carefully the instrument you require according to what is fitting.
dou feu	by fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	Gangrene occurs either due to an internal cause or an external one; and when you have treated this decay with medicinal remedies, and they do not succeed, then it is necessary to cut off that limb up to the point where the decay reaches, so that the patient escapes death through this means, or avoids a greater harm from the loss of the limb; the sign of it is that the limb becomes black, so that it seems as if it has been burned by fire, and then rots after turning black, as this corruption can spread from one limb to another and reach throughout the body; so hasten with the cutting, and if it is due to the sting of venomous creatures, such as a sea scorpion or viper or the like, if the decay is at the tip of a finger, then cut it off, and do not allow it to spread down to the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And if the corruption reaches the hand, then cut it at the joint, so that the decay does not spread to the arm; and if it reaches the arm, then cut it at the elbow; and if it passes the elbow, it is death, and no external remedy is of any use except the measure of its power; and do likewise if the decay reaches the foot: if it reaches the first joint, then cut it after the second joint; and if it reaches the foot, then cut off the entire foot; and if it rises up to the leg, then cut at the knee joint; and if it goes above the knee, then there is no other solution but to leave the patient to die; and the manner of cutting or sawing the limb is this: tie it above and below, and let one assistant hold one binding downwards, and another assistant hold the other binding upwards, and then separate the flesh that is between the two bindings to a breadth of one handspan, so that the bone is exposed; then cut or saw it, and place a piece of linen on each side, so that the saw does not touch the healthy area, to prevent further injury or the formation of a hot abscess in the patient.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And if a flow of blood occurs while you are working, then cauterize the area immediately, or apply some hemostatic powders; then return to your treatment until it is complete, then bind the wounded limb with an appropriate bandage, and care for it until it is healed; and I will tell you a story about what happened to a man with his foot: he developed a blackening that seemed like a burn from fire, and this decay began first in his toe, until it took over the entire foot; and when the man saw the decay, he hastened to cut off his foot, and he was healed; and a long time after, the decay returned to a finger on his hand, and he came to me, and I applied counteracting treatments after purifying his body, but the decay would not stop; and he wanted me to cut off his hand, but I would not, because I had hope of dispelling the matter; and I also feared that if I amputated his hand, he might die, for the man’s strength was weak; and he despaired entirely, and returned to his land, and hastened to cut off his own hand, and he was healed; and I have recounted this story only so that one may act similarly, if one should have need.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	Sometimes an abscess forms in a fleshy area and remains so long that it creates a large collection of pus; then it ruptures and breaks open, and the pus spurts out, leaving the area empty, like a hollow vessel; and the skin above is as thin as a delicate cloth, yet it does not extend to the bone or the nerve, and such a condition is called a "sain," and is not called a "fistula." But if it extends so deeply that it reaches the bone, then it is called a "fistula"; and in such cases, the treatment is to cut away the entire surrounding skin, especially when it is as thin as a cloth; and it does not harden due to its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if you are confident that the skin is hardened, and the corruption is not deep, and the skin is thick with flesh, then treat it with a cleansing enema in the following way: observe if the swelling is large and the discharge that comes out is of a foul odor, then cauterize it with Egyptian medicine prepared in this way: take garlic, oil, and litharge in equal parts, and let it cook in a vessel over the fire until the medicine is red and thick as honey; then take what you need of it, dissolve it in water and honey, and cleanse the swelling, sealing the opening; and leave the medicine in for two hours, then extract it by pressing; do this many times until the swelling is purified and the stench is removed. At times, you may cleanse with ash water if this medicine is not available; to do so, take ashes from vine wood, pour water over them, strain it, and use it to cleanse until you are certain the swelling is thoroughly purified. If the patient cannot tolerate the Egyptian medicine or ash water, then cleanse with water and honey with a little crushed litharge; or cleanse with honey mixed with wine, since honey has the property of purifying and washing, while wine makes the swelling contract; and when you have done this, and you are confident that the swelling is well purified, then cleanse it with a treatment that promotes the growth of flesh in it, which is to take diachylon plaster, and mix it with rose oil and wine; or cleanse it with certain medicines and ointments whose properties I have described in the treatise on ointments. If the opening of the swelling is narrow, and the nozzle of the enema cannot enter, then enlarge it a little with a heated instrument, and insert a tent of Egyptian ointment or basilicon ointment until it is widened; and if the wound is too wide, sew it up, leaving only an opening for the enema nozzle to enter; and if the opening where the discharge exits is above, then make an incision at a lower point.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	For when the pus is deep, it does not allow flesh to regenerate there; and if you are unable to cut out the swelling from below as you would like, then arrange it in such a way that the pus flows to the lowest point present, for when the pus is deep, it prevents flesh from regenerating. If you cannot cut out the swelling from below as you intend, then proceed in this way: allow the pus to flow easily downward, and do not leave any pus behind; and take consolidative medicines to apply over the swelling, spreading them onto a piece of linen that will cover the entire swelling. Then, make a cut slightly larger than the initial opening of the swelling, then spread a soft ointment onto another cloth according to the size of the opening, and place it over the swelling to help the pus drain, without removing the larger cloth except once after many days; and frequently remove the one covering the opening of the swelling to remove the pus, and observe what type of pus flows out—whether it is venomous or little or much, digested or undigested; and take note if the patient feels pain or not, if there is an abscess or not, and when your treatment has been applied in this way and you see that new tissue is forming at the opening of the swelling, know that the swelling is already beginning to heal and recovery is near. Then remove the dressing in the morning, or on the third day, and when you undress the wound, change to a fresh cloth, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the swelling continues to discharge undigested pus after many days, know that the swelling is not healing.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if thin, refined pus flows after a long time, do not despair of recovery, for healing is near.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	For there are people whose wounds are slow to generate flesh, and others with the opposite condition; and if an undigested humor emerges from the sinus after many days, know that the sinus has not yet closed up; and if the sinus is slow to close and remains open, then add medicines that are moist in substance and dry in virtue, such as the ointment "diaphenite," which contains a large amount of vitriol and is a final remedy. Take the diaphenite ointment and mix it with rose oil, sprinkle it with old wine in equal measure, then prepare it and apply it; and the same can be done using thick, well-cooked honey when diaphenite ointment is not available, or you can take myrrh, aloe, and frankincense, grind them, and sprinkle the powder onto the honey when it is over the fire; then soak a cloth in it, spread it over the sinus, and sometimes add aristolochia longa and roots of the heavenly lily, which resembles the flour of vetch and centaury; and use these as either simple or compound medicines: grind them to a powder, place it on the honey as I have described, and apply it; and if the treatment is prolonged, and the sinus is not healed by this treatment, then know that the infection has penetrated deeply and has affected the bone, or the hard tissues, or the ligaments; in that case, treat it as you would treat a fistula, as we have explained above.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	On the swelling of the nail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	Panarice is a swelling that arises under the nail of the hand's thumb, or of the foot, or sometimes appears on other fingers; and when it has aged and gone untreated, a hot swelling arises there, and it flows and expels pus until it reaches the root of the nail, and sometimes it destroys the entire nail; the corrosion reaches the bone, bringing foul pain, and the tip of the finger swells, and the color is dusky.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and if the treatment does not succeed, it is necessary that you cut with iron all the excess that remains of the nail, then cauterize the wound afterward.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	The cautery is very helpful if the bone is healthy, and the nail is sound; and if the nail presses into the flesh, pricking it and wounding it, you must place a wedge under the nail that pricks the flesh, lifting it, and cut that flesh delicately and lightly, and apply burning and corrosive medicines to remove everything; then treat it with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if the corrosion is in the bone, then cut it and remove the rot, for as long as the corrupted bone remains, it cannot heal; and if you see the finger decaying, then cut it at one of the joints as has been said before, then treat it until it is healed; and if it is swollen and inflamed, and the pain is intense, you must drain it first; then cut the nail with a sharp scalpel, slicing across, and ensure the cut does not reach the flesh beneath the nail, for the patient would feel too much pain; if it does happen, place something on it to soothe the pain.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The pain of the sixth finger of the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The extra finger that grows on the hands of some men is sometimes fully fleshy, and sometimes it has a bit of bone, and sometimes a nail, and some of them grow at the root of the joint, or the growth is at one of the joints of the fingers.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	The one that grows at some knuckle of the finger does not move, and the one that grows at the joint of the finger can sometimes move; the cutting of the fleshy one is easy, as follows: cut it at its root with a wide scalpel.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	The one that grows at the root of the joint is difficult to treat: so refrain from cutting.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In the one that grows on the finger at the last joint, you must first cut the flesh in a rounded manner down to the bone, then cut the bone with an appropriate saw, then treat it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The fusing that happens to fingers joined together occurs by birth, or by fusion of a wound, or by burning with fire, or by similar causes.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	You must then cut that fusion so that the fingers regain their natural shape; then place between them cloths or bandages moistened with rose oil so that they do not fuse together again; or place between them thin pieces of lead until the area is fully healed, as required.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If the fusion occurs between one of these fingers and the palm, then cut that fusion as needed.
des vils	On swollen veins
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	The swollen veins are large, inflamed veins full of melancholy excess, which appear in several parts of the body; they appear more often in the legs of those who walk, work, and carry burdens than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Thus, you must sometimes administer a purgative for bile, and then bleed the basilica vein.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The treatment with iron is in two ways: one is that you cut them, and draw out the black blood; the other way is that you raise the vein, and extract it entirely.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The cutting is done as follows: first bathe the leg with very hot water until the thick blood thins, then compress the leg of the patient from above the thigh down to the area below the knee; then cut the vein in one place, or two or three, with a large incision, then raise and draw out the black blood by hand, from one end to the other, until as much blood is expelled as the patient’s strength can bear; then bind it, and instruct him to abstain from foods that produce black bile; and repeat the draining and bleeding when the veins are full and harm the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The procedure is as follows: raise the leg of the patient. If there is much hair, then place it in a bath and pour warm water over the leg until it turns red and the veins swell. If you do not have a bath, warm it by the fire instead. Then cut lengthwise along the vein from the top of the knee or at the part below the ankle. Open the skin along the vein with a lancet and scrape the vein from each side until it becomes visible to the touch; it will appear red and black, and when it enters the skin it looks like a white cord. Then insert a thread underneath until it is lifted from the skin, and then suspend it lightly with a hook. Make another incision three finger-widths higher, scrape the skin over the vein until it appears, lift it with a thread as before, and suspend it on another hook as you did the first time. Make another cut—or more, as needed—then lift it and cut at the toe. Then pull and lift up to the second incision, then extract it from cut to cut until it is entirely out; then cut it. If you cannot pull and lift it, insert a needle with a strong double thread, tie it, pull it, and insert a hook beneath, then twist your hand back and forth until it comes out. Take care not to cut it, for if it breaks, you will not be able to pull or lift it, and this will be harmful to the patient. When you have fully extracted it, place on the wound moistened wool soaked in wine and rose oil, and treat it until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if the vein is twisted and contorted and tangled together, and it is not straight as we have said, you must then split it along its twists, but do not cut it; and draw it out as we have previously described.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	The shape of the iron tool used to cut the vein is curved and not sharpened, so it does not sever the vein; it is of a thick curve, for if it were thin, it would cut the vein, but it must be thick as we have said, and this is the shape:
de la voinne civile	On the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein appears in the legs, in hot regions where no grass or trees grow, and in lands where there is no moisture; and sometimes it arises elsewhere than in the legs, and this occurs from the decay that appears under the skin, just as serpents and worms appear within the body, generated between the skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And the sign of the onset of this vein is that a very great inflammation appears in the leg, then the area changes, and the vein begins to come out like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	When the tip appears, you must wrap around it a piece of lead from one and a half to two ounces, and tie it, leaving the lead hanging from the leg, and each time it pushes out a bit further, wrap it around the lead and tie it; if it becomes too long, cut off a part and wrap the remainder, but do not cut it at the root until it is completely out; for if you cut it, it will retreat into the flesh and cause swelling and decay in the area, and serious illness; thus it is necessary to draw it out little by little until the end, so nothing remains in the body; sometimes this vein, when drawn out, is five handspans long, or even ten, and once a man came to me with it extending ten handspans, and when you cut it, place a rod or a tube, and pierce it down to the base, so that everything can come out; and empty out the matter that is within, and apply decay-preventing medicines to the area for a few days, then treat it as with swellings.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And sometimes this vein has several branches, especially when it appears at the joint of the foot, or in the foot, and there are many openings, and from them branches sprout; treat it then as we have described above.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	On worms that grow between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This illness is called in our land “ox disease,” because it often happens to oxen, and it is a small worm that grows between the skin and flesh, and it moves throughout the body, rising and descending, and one can feel it traveling from limb to limb, until it pierces the skin wherever it goes, and emerges; it is generated from the decay of certain humors, as worms, serpents, earthworms, and ascarids appear in the abdomen; it is feared for its malice, for when it moves through the body, and if it rises to the head and reaches the eye, it may enter and destroy the eye; and this happens often.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you want to treat and remove it, it can only be drawn out when it is moving: you must then bind the area above and below with a strong, tight binding, then cut above and draw it out, and if the worm is deep in the flesh and you cannot find it, cauterize above with fire until it dies; the greatest harm it causes is that it invades the eye, as we have said; and if you see it approaching the head near the eye, press down tightly on the brow below it, then cut above and draw it out; and the patient must use body-purifying medicines that dissolve the corrupted humors, and avoid foods that produce decay.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	Of the pain that comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This illness is called "vakirir" in our land, and it is a pain that comes in certain limbs, and then moves from limb to limb; and I saw what I tell you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called to a sick woman, and she uncovered her arm for me, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of her arm; and shortly afterward, I saw it rise like a worm to her shoulder, faster than anything, just like quicksilver when it runs from one place to another; the pain left that spot, and settled in her shoulder, and then shortly after ran through her whole body, until it came to the other arm; then she told me that it always turned around her body, as I saw.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marveled greatly at how it moved thus from limb to limb, for I had never seen this illness in such a manner.
