Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	Nevertheless, I had seen many who indeed had pain move from one place to another, but I had never seen it as I saw it in this woman; and I thought to myself that it was because the woman had a dry body and uncovered veins, and for this reason, this constrained windiness appeared; and this does not appear for those who are soft, and who have moist bodies and covered veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you wish to cure this illness, and the sick person feels this pain, if it appears to you as we have said, then bind it above and below quickly, and then cut upon it until that constrained windiness escapes from the spot; and cauterize the spot; and if you do not see it with your eyes, treat it with that which expels windiness, such as fetid pills, pills of serapin, and other similar remedies.
des saiettes	Of the arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are varied, according to their appearances and according to the places on the body where they fall.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	Their diversity is such that there are some which have large points, and small ones, some with heads, and some soldered; some with two edges, some with blades, and some with pieces; and the one that falls in any limb falls in two ways: either in a principal limb like the brain, heart, liver, lung, kidneys, intestines, bladder, and similar organs.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When it falls in one of these places, and the signs of death, which I will tell you later, appear: then you must beware of extracting this arrow, for death follows in many conditions; and when these evil signs do not appear, and the arrow is not deeply embedded, then pull it out, and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the signs in the brain when the arrow falls there and pierces the bone, and makes the fluid above the brain escape, are when there is dizziness and deafness and whirling and redness in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasm and confusion of the mind, and vomiting of bile; and sometimes fluid flows from the nostrils, or from the ears; and sometimes speech and voice are lost; and from the wound emerges white moisture like pus, and also oozing flesh; and if these signs appear, refrain from treating it, and extract the arrow if it is not deeply embedded.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The signs of the arrow when it falls in the heart are that it is near the left breast, and feels as if it were stuck in something hard, not empty; and sometimes the arrow moves like the pulse, and black blood flows, and coldness and cold sweat come, and fainting: know then without doubt that death is descending.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of an arrow that pierces the lung is that foam-filled blood spurts from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient changes color, sighs deeply, and seeks cool air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow falls into the covering of the chest, it is near the small ribs; and he takes deep breaths and has great pain and sighs; and all the limbs of the shoulders move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow falls in the stomach, sometimes something of the undigested food spurts from the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow falls in the belly, and some dung comes out through the route of the intestines, then there is no hope for treatment, nor for extracting the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow falls in the bladder, and urine spurts out and flows externally, and the patient feels intense pain: know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other parts, such as the face, neck, throat, shoulders, joints, spine, chest, thighs, legs, and similar members, are safe depending on various conditions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery, and it is not venomous, as I will tell you from what happened to me, so that you may do likewise.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	It happened to a man that an arrow fell into his tear duct at the root of his nose: I examined it, and extracted it from the other side below the fat of his ear, and he was healed without any harm.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And I extracted from an eye an arrow that had fallen into the fat below the lower eyelid, and the arrow was embedded, and I could only reach the point near the shaft, and the arrow was large from a Turkish bow, with a light iron head without barbs; the eye was healed, and no bad effects followed.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And I extracted an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and it was an Arabian arrow with barbs: I smoothed the barbs, and with great care I extracted it, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And I extracted an arrow from a man, which had fallen in his belly, and I thought he would die; but after thirty days had passed, and his condition had not changed, I made an incision over the arrow, carefully maneuvered it, and extracted it, and there was no bad outcome.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And I saw a man in whom an arrow had fallen in his back, and the wound had healed over; the arrow remained inside him, and his natural condition did not change, nor was there any harm in his natural functions.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And I saw another man, in whom an arrow had fallen into his face, and the wound healed; and he remained in this state without suffering great pain; and many others like this.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And I extracted an arrow from a man among the king’s princes, which had fallen in the middle of his nose, and was inclined a little to the right; and the arrow was fully embedded. I was called to treat it after it had been in for three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I probed it with a fine probe, and could not feel it; but he felt a prickling and pain below his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was from the arrow’s point. I applied an attractive and digestive poultice to the spot so that the area would not swell; and the location of the arrow appeared.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I applied the poultice for several days, and the wound healed again, and the patient remained in this state for a long time, until one day he felt the arrow inside his nose; and he told me.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I applied a strong corrosive medicine to the wound for several days, until it was open, and I probed it, and felt the arrow’s tip fixed in the spot; then I continued applying the medicine into the wound’s opening until the arrow’s head visibly appeared; and a period of about four months passed, and then I enlarged the wound enough to insert pincers, and moved it from side to side, but it would not come out; so I continued to refine and maneuver different instruments until one day I grasped it with well-made pincers, in the way whose form will come at the end of this chapter, until I extracted it, and restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And the physicians believe that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored: I restored it then, and the wound healed, and the patient was entirely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	Now I have told you the quality of the extraction of certain arrows, so that you place your care on what I do not mention, for the book cannot cover everything; but the wise master compares a great thing from very little, and from what is present and what is lacking, finds new technique, and new instrument, for the descent of strange things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows do not exit the limbs in which they are embedded except in two ways: either through the place where they enter, or through another part; and those that exit through where they enter are arrows embedded in fleshy areas, and sometimes come out immediately.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it [the arrow] does not come out immediately, leave it until the flesh around it decays, making the extraction easier; and similarly, if it is embedded in the bone and cannot come out, leave it in for a few days, moving it each day. Then it will come out, and if it does not, drill around it with a fine bit until the area around it is widened, and then extract it.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if the arrow is embedded in the bone of the head and reaches one of the ventricles of the brain, and any of the symptoms I have mentioned appear in the patient: do not extract it, but leave it until it stabilizes after a few days, for if the arrow reaches the meningeal layer (syfac), it is fatal.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is only embedded in the bone, and does not reach the meningeal layer, and the patient remains for a few days without bad symptoms, then carefully attempt to extract it.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is deeply embedded and cannot be removed, use borers around it, as I have told you; then treat the area until it heals.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	If the arrow is embedded in a part of the body where it cannot be seen, search for it with a probe; if you feel it, use an appropriate instrument to extract it. If you cannot due to the wound’s narrowness or the arrow’s depth, and there is no bone, nerve, or vein in the way, make an incision to enlarge the wound. Extract the arrow if you can, and if it has barbs that are holding it in place, cut away the flesh around it on both sides as best as you can, then break or bend the barbs on the arrow so that you can extract it. Be very careful not to break the arrow, as this would make the extraction more difficult.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot extract it at once, leave it until the surrounding area decays, then extract it, as the extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	If the blood flow works against you, administer the treatments we discussed in its chapter; avoid incising nerves and veins, and use ingenuity in how you extract the arrow safely, whether quickly or slowly, or firmly or gently. Position the patient as he was when the arrow fell into him, as this is the greatest help, and if you cannot, position him as the signs indicate.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	When an arrow is coming out the other side, or part of it is visible, or the skin is swollen there so that it is visibly or palpably apparent: make an incision there, enough for the pincers to grip it, and then extract it. Then it will come out immediately.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held in the bone, rotate your hand around it until it goes into the bone and enlarges it, then extract it.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot come out, leave it in again, then resume extraction until it comes out; if the shaft of the arrow is still attached, push on it with the shaft; if the shaft has broken off, and you wish to apply force, use an instrument with a socket, so that the point of the arrow enters into the socket of the instrument; then push it out. If the arrow is broken, insert a pointed instrument to help with the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is poisoned, you must cut away all the flesh around where the venom is, if possible, then treat the wound as necessary.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrow falls into the foot, or the belly, or the bladder, or the side, and it is close to the surface, and you can cut above it, then cut; take care not to cut veins or nerves, then extract it, then sew up the wound, if needed, and treat it until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The form of the pincers used to extract arrows is similar to the beak of a bird, and here is the form:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many types: large, medium, and small, depending on the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the socketed pushing tool is like the feather of a bird, used to push on the arrow’s point, as here is the form:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the form of the pincers for pushing and pulling is as follows:
des voinnes dou cors communes	Of the common veins of the body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	Of the veins from which one bleeds, there are thirty-one, of which sixteen are in the head, namely: two beating veins behind the ears, which are called the two “herbech”; the two arteries that are visible in the temples; and two veins in the tear ducts of the eyes, which are called “aspires”; the vein that is in the middle of the forehead; the vein at the bridge of the nose; the two "guindeges" in the neck; the two veins above the lips, called the “augeherich”; and two veins beneath the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The veins from which one commonly bleeds are five in each arm: one is the cephalic vein, located on the left side, and it is called by laymen the “head vein”; the middle one is called the “faste,” formed by the cephalic and basilic, and laymen call it the “heart vein”; the basilic is on the right side, called by laymen the “belly vein,” and lies above the armpit, visible and from which bleeding is done, clearly seen over the pocket.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And the “salvatelle” is the vein located between the ring finger and little finger, and it has two branches; in the leg and foot there are three veins: one is beneath the curve of the pocket on the left side, the second is the “sophene” at the ankle on the right side; and the vein called “nesse,” which is at the ankle on the other side; and on the other leg are three veins beneath these.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The bleeding of the veins behind the ears helps with old cataracts and migraine; the procedure for bleeding, as I tell you, is that you raise the head of the patient, rub the place of the veins with a rough cloth; then the patient tightens his neck with a vise, until the two veins appear behind the ears in two places extending from the head: locate them with your finger, and where you feel the pulse under your finger, bleed there; then take the lancet, place it below the vein until reaching the bone, lift your hand with the vein upwards, and cut both the skin and the vein across the width of two fingers, and let the blood flow as much as you wish; then press and bind, until it is healed; and I have already mentioned the incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	The bleeding of the two arteries in the temples is beneficial for old migraine, sudden attacks, chronic eye inflammation, and acute tearing in the eyes; the method for bleeding is as I tell you: the patient tightens his neck until the two veins clearly appear; feel the pulse under your finger, and then bleed there; then raise the heart over the vein upwards with your index finger, place the lancet underneath, lift the vein upwards, and cut it, as you did with the other two veins, and let the blood flow as needed; then loosen the patient, place your finger over the vein for one hour, then apply cotton; and then bind it tightly, leaving it until it heals; we have already spoken about their cutting and extraction at the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The bleeding of the vein in the forehead is as effective as the bleeding of the cephalic vein for old ailments of the face, migraines, and redness; and the method is for the patient to twist his neck until the vein appears; then take the instrument called “fosseur,” of which here is the form:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	Place the tip on the vein, press with your hand, or with something else, and let the blood flow according to the quantity you want; then loosen the patient’s neck, bind the vein until it is healed; sometimes it is done with a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, the flame should not be too sharp; bleed across it, as the bone is nearby, and sometimes the flame breaks when it is too thin.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The bleeding of the two veins in the tear ducts helps the eyes, against ringworm, redness, styes in the eye, and diseases of the face; and the method for their bleeding is that the patient tightens his neck by twisting it with a band, as before; then bleed him, and let the bleeding be transverse, a little longer with a slightly wide lancet, because there is no flesh there.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the lancet is too thin, it may break; then let the blood flow as much as needed, then place cotton over it, and bind it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The bleeding of the vein in the nose is good for acute fever, sudden frenzy, and diseases of the face, such as migraines and redness that appears on the face, especially when it is chronic; the method for bleeding is that the patient tightens his neck, then you press his nose with your left hand, and take the fine, long lancet, inserting it into the lip in the space between the two nostrils, because the vein is not clearly visible there, and the blood will start to flow immediately; do not go too deep, and let the blood flow according to necessity, then bind it for a night, for it heals very quickly; and this is the form of the lancet.
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The bleeding of the two "guindeges" veins helps with tightness of breath, the onset of leprosy, many diseases, impetigo, corrosive sores, herpes, and swollen glands; the method for bleeding is that the patient tightens his neck below each, as we have said; the master stands over the patient’s head, and the patient sits on a seat, then bleed the vein lengthwise a little broadly, then let blood flow slowly, or as much as needed; repeat on the other vein, then loosen the band, pressing on both veins moderately so that the patient does not choke; leave it until morning, until the wound is healed.
de la sainie des leivres	On bleeding from the lips
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The bleeding of the veins in the upper lips helps with oral scurvy, gum decay, chapped lips, and sores around the nose and mouth.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the method for bleeding is to have the patient sit in front of you and tighten his neck as I have said; then turn the lip, and look at the two veins, one in the right lip and the other in the left, known by their blackness, and by the fine black veins around them: then cut both, and if you do not know them or are in doubt, cut the largest one on each side, and do the same with the two veins above and below, as it is the same procedure.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	On bleeding beneath the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The bleeding of the veins beneath the tongue helps after bleeding the cephalic vein, and it is good for throat tightness, diseases of the uvula, and mouth diseases; and the method for bleeding is that the patient sits in your hands facing the sun, lifts his tongue, and you look below it on each side for a black vein: bleed both, but do not go too deep, as the arteries are below.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins of the elbow from which one commonly bleeds are bled in two ways: either by pricking with a wide lancet called a “mirtin” or a thin, sharp lancet called an “olivaire” that cuts like a knife, also called “anesil”; they vary in width and fineness according to the size and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the “mirtin” lancet is very well-known and is wide, as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	It is needed to open swollen veins full of thick, visible blood, containing thick and cloudy blood; and this is the form of the “olivaire” lancet:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	It is more finely pointed, and is used to bleed finer veins, where there is fine, yellowish blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The bleeding of the basilic vein, which is one of these veins, helps with diseases below the throat, in the neck, chest, and abdomen. The practitioner must bleed cautiously and be wary of the artery that lies beneath it.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	If the artery is cut and there is excessive bleeding, it must be stopped as I have previously explained. The lancet should not be pricking but cutting, like an "anesil" blade.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	If the basilic vein is not clearly visible, you should tighten it, making another vein stand out, or seek any branch of it, or bleed in its place the vein in the middle of the arm, which is clearly visible, and cut it with the "anesil" lancet, as we have described.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	If you want to locate the site for bleeding, before tightening the arm, touch the spot until you feel the pulse, then mark the spot with ink. Bind the arm, then cut the vein with the "anesil" lancet. Take care not to strike the artery if you see the area swell, as that indicates the artery is there; avoid it then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	If you see the blood spurting upward like a child’s urine, and the blood is red and thin, know that it is arterial blood. Quickly press your finger on it for a long time, and then remove your finger if the blood stops, which often happens. Bind the arm, and leave it as is, ensuring the patient does not move it; keep watch and ensure he does not move it until it is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	If the blood does not stop and overcomes you, and if no remedy is available, cut the artery if it is visible, for its ends will retract; and the bleeding will be stopped.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	Then take a bark of mastic, split it, take one half, and bind it well over the wound until the next day. If the bleeding stops, that is good; if not, treat it as previously described, with powders that staunch blood. The stopping of blood is not difficult in most situations due to the small size of the wound and the tightness of the binding on the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The bleeding of the median vein helps by drawing blood from the head above and from the body below, as it is connected to both the basilic and cephalic veins, as we have said. The practitioner must be cautious of the nerve that lies below it, for if he goes too deep and strikes the nerve, it will swell, the pain will be severe, and it may not heal. This nerve is often visible, but if it is not visible in some people due to its fineness, then you should bleed with the "anesil" tool and avoid the nerve as much as possible.
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	If there is a vein between two nerves, then cut it lengthwise.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The bleeding of the cephalic vein helps by drawing blood from the head and benefits the eyes; it should be bled by pricking with the "olivaire" or "mirtin" lancet, as it is the safest of all veins, having neither a nerve nor an artery beneath it.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	Nevertheless, it is necessary to find the lightest spot, and it does not matter if the first attempt fails, as you can try again; sometimes the site may swell in some people if the first attempt fails, but this is not a problem.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The method of bleeding should follow your judgment.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you should know about bleeding is that it should only be performed to maintain health and to prevent future diseases; it should be done in one of the three veins in the elbow: the cephalic, the median, and the basilic. Bleeding should be done at the beginning of spring on an empty stomach, and in autumn and winter after eating, when signs of fullness appear; and it should be done on the first or third day, after two or three hours of daylight.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	Bleeding administered for illnesses has no set time and should be done whenever needed, day or night, at any hour and in any season; children under 14 years should not be bled, nor should pregnant women, except from the fourth to the seventh month.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	And elderly people over the age of 60 should not be bled.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when someone wishes to be bled, in whatever manner it may be, it is necessary to cleanse the intestines with a light enema if much feces is retained, so that the veins do not draw harmful putrid excess from the intestines to the principal organs. Nor should someone who is overly full of food, or drunk to the point of losing reason, nor anyone suffering from dropsy be bled. And bleeding should be avoided after an episode of colic, vomiting, diarrhea, frequent intercourse, exertion, sleeplessness, fasting, and anything that diminishes strength, either of spirit or of body. Then, thin the humors, if the blood is thick, by means of food, drink, and medicines, if you have the means; then enter the bath, if nothing forbids it, to thin the blood, and bleed yourself from the vein of the breast around the third rib, as we have mentioned. And guard yourself on that day from work, effort, lust, and similar things, and be calm and joyful. The one performing the bleeding should be higher than the one being bled, and should rub the arm two or three times, then moderately tighten the binding above, for if it is too tight or too loose, the blood cannot flow. Then rub the place with the hands until the veins swell and can be felt. Then the one performing the bleeding moistens the lancet with a little old oil, then places the finger of his left hand slightly above the place where he wants to bleed, so the vein does not slip and fail to be struck.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	For there are veins that flee like strings under the lancet, and some are full of air, so that when the flame is applied, it draws the flame back, and the vein cannot open, and so it is with these; and if the vein opens, the wound is too narrow, therefore the bleeder must be cautious of these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein opens the first time, that is good; if not, then start again a little below that place or above it quickly, if the place is not swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the place is swollen, and the patient is afraid, leave it for a day or two, and do not bind the arm: perhaps a warm swelling will come; do not enter a bath, then restart the bleeding if it pleases him; and if the opening is small, or the blood flows subtly and you doubt that as much blood comes out as you want, then press into that same opening with the flame directly; and open it quickly, before the place swells; for this happens often when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the place swell, do not restart the bleeding, and apply a little oil dregs, for it soothes the flow of blood, and it is better to use dregs than oil on this spot; and thus apply the oil dregs to each bleeding that you bleed the veins, to stop the flow of blood; and theriac and borage do the same, when applied to the spot; it refines the blood and disperses it when it is too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if a large swelling appears, which happens often, especially when it was only bled at that time or the opening of the vein is small, hurry, and apply a sponge soaked in water and a little warm salt, and squeeze it for an hour; and do this after the blood flow from the vein, and if any blackness or greenness remains at the site after some days, it does no harm; and if you wish, apply something of aloe or myrrh softened in calament juice, mustard, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And often a swelling and appearance occurs at the bleeding of the basilic vein: then place your hand on it, and if you find the place soft under the pressure of the hand, that appearance is bad.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Avoid then applying anything of what we have said, for perhaps blood will flow from the artery; but make a dry plaster to harden the place, then treat it with another treatment, until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And draw blood from each according to the quantity of his strength and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the blood is black, let it flow until it is red; and if you see it thick, let it flow until it becomes thin; and if it is too hot, let it cool.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And it is necessary for the one who is full and strong, and needs bloodletting, to make a larger wound, and the flame should be wide; and for the one who is weak, do the opposite, and he should be bled little and often, and should be bled by cutting crosswise, not by pricking; and this way of bleeding is safer from blood loss and nerve damage, and is worth more than bleeding lengthwise or broadly.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And for the one whose body fails during bleeding, give bread soaked in pomegranate juice; if he is warmed, bleed him three or four times. And if he has a cold complexion, eat beforehand bread soaked in aged syrup, or syrup of aromatic honey with spices, such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chickpeas, and a pleasantly fragrant syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if he faints from the bleeding, after the issue of much blood, it is necessary that he inhale meat broth, and a delicate fragrant syrup, and use the other things we have said in the section or chapter on fainting, for the evacuation of the vein.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wishes to ventilate his arm, and bleed again, it is necessary, when he is weakened by heavy bleeding, that he bleed himself little by little, according to the quantity of his strength continuously.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And he who wishes to ventilate his arm after the first bleeding, and has a strong body, should bleed himself seven hours after the first bleeding, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And he who wishes to be bled again in another place should be bled on the second or third day.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	For there is much blood in the body that is already warmed and causes fever; a large quantity must be drawn, and the opening enlarged so that he may fall into faintness; then review all the conditions of bleeding, and place your hand on his pulse while he bleeds, so that death does not come in place of faintness, and this happens often when the bleeder is negligent; and it is not fitting, when you want to unbind the arm and let the blood flow a second time, and the opening is closed, that you press hard upon it; nor, if it is bent, should he extend the arm hastily, for that would be harmful; but leave it until he bleeds a second time; or you may prick it with the tip of the lancet, so that the blood which has clotted at the vein's opening may come out, and apply a little salt mixed in water, and press upon it lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, leave it and do not bind it, until the swelling subsides.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if it is necessary to draw blood a second time, bleed him in the same place, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein in the middle of the arm is bled in place of the vein of the head because it is composed that way.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the manner of bleeding is that the patient puts his hand in hot water until the small veins are red; then bind it moderately, so that the veins appear well, then bleed him immediately crosswise, not broad nor long; and let the opening be large, and bleed him very near the joint of the hand, and if blood cannot flow from it, put the hand back in hot water, and let the blood run in the water until you have enough; and if it is summer, do not put the hand back in hot water, for it is done more in winter than in summer; and the bleeding from this vein is safer than from any other veins, for there is no artery or nerve there.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The bleeding of the salvatella vein in the right hand is beneficial for all diseases of the liver, and it is done this way: squeeze the hand, and put it in hot water until the veins are swollen so that they are visible; and bleed it crosswise, and if you cut it entirely, it does no harm; do not go too deep, for the nerves are entirely uncovered by flesh below, and then put the hand back in hot water if the blood clots in the wound, and cannot flow out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have drawn as much blood as needed, then put oil and salt on the vein to close it quickly, and do this with each vein.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The bleeding of it in the left hand is beneficial for spleen disease, and do just as I told you on the right side.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The bleeding of the saphenous vein is beneficial for all diseases below the body, such as diseases of the womb, retention of menstrual blood, and diseases of the loins, thighs, and old afflictions of the legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the method of its bleeding is that the patient puts his foot in hot water, and rubs the vein until it appears, and binds it above the ankle joint; and the vein is at the ankle, and above the foot run many branches; then bleed it either in the larger branch or at the ankle, which is very effective.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you bleed it on the foot, beware of the nerves beneath, and bleed it crosswise as if cutting; and let the lancet be thin.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the blood cannot flow out, then put the foot back in the water, and let the vein empty well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the bleeder fails the first time, start again a little above, for the place is safe; do not fear the nerve, as we have said, and do likewise for the saphenous vein of the other foot as well.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The site of the sciatic vein is at the ankle outside, and bleeding it is good for hip pain, when it is due to hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And the nature of this bloodletting is that the patient enters the bath and presses above the ankle with four fingers, twisting, for otherwise the vein does not appear; and if it appears, then bleed it in all the ways you can, and by crossing; and it is often good to cut it, because the place is safe, and it is much recommended for many people.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you do not find it, then bleed any branch of it that appears on the back of the foot, and towards the little toe, and be careful of the nerves; and let the blood flow as much as you want, then loosen the tie, put cotton on it, and press it; it is then healed.
des sainies de ventouse	On the bloodletting by cupping
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Cups are made of horns, or brass, or glass; and cupping is done in two ways: either by piercing and drawing blood, or without piercing.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this cupping, which is without piercing, is done in two ways: either with fire or without fire; and the cupping that is done by piercing and drawing blood is done in fourteen places on the body, of which one is at the top of the head; another is in the middle of the neck; two others are on both sides of the neck; a cup below the chin; cups on both shoulders; cups on the buttocks; cups in the middle of both arms; cups on both legs; cups on both ankles; and this cupping does not draw blood except from the small veins that are spread in the flesh, and for this reason it does not weaken one, as is done by vein bloodletting; and it is not necessary that it be administered, either with fire or without fire, in any illness that comes from overfilling, until the whole body has been emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if by necessity of illness it is necessary to cup, or by custom, then we will administer it at each hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and in the middle and in each season; for there are those who, when they need to cup, have a heavy head; and there are some who find fullness and redness in their face, and in their head, and in the neck, and dimness in their eyes; and those who find a drop of blood in their mouth, and have a swollen tongue, and spit blood; and there are those who dream and see by night blood and wounded and dead and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and especially when it is the middle of the month, we order him to be cupped after the third hour of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The bloodletting of the head vein helps the heaviness of the head … which comes to the eyes, and it is not necessary that it be after the evacuation of the whole body; and this cupping is in place of the cephalic bloodletting, and it is not necessary for one who has a cold temperament to use it, or one who has catarrh, for it greatly harms them; and therefore it is not necessary for the elderly to use it, nor those who have cold ailments in the head.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And he who often bleeds himself becomes forgetful, and therefore it is necessary to place the cup a little lower, for fear of forgetfulness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	The cupping in the middle of the neck is in place of the bloodletting of the head and basilic veins, and for this it is effective for tightness of the chest, and for the splitting of the bronchial channel, and for cough, and for fullness; it must be placed gently, for if it holds too firmly, it causes forgetfulness or disturbance of the stomach and heart.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	The cupping on both sides of the neck is effective for head pains, for eye ailments and migraines, for strangulation, and for pain at the roots of the teeth, and it is in place of the basilic bloodletting; and you must instruct the practitioner to press his hand when applying it, so that he does not cut the artery, and there is no hemorrhaging.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	The cupping below the chin is effective for ailments of the mouth, for gum disease, and similar ailments that are in the mouth; and it is in place of bloodletting of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The cupping on the shoulders is effective for illnesses that come from heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	The cupping of the elbows is as effective as that of the three veins of the arm, for it draws blood from these large veins; and instruct the practitioner not to pierce too deeply, for the place is bare of flesh, and there are nerves and arteries below.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The cup placed on the rump is effective for hemorrhoids at the base and for diseases below, and the cup should be large and made of brass, as it needs to draw well; and by chance, if it were thin, it would break; and it makes large wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The cupping of the legs bleeds openly, for it draws blood from the whole body, and is effective for chronic pains of the loins, the womb, and the bladder, and it reduces menstruation; and it is in place of the two saphenous veins and the two ankles, and yet it weakens the body after long use and causes faintness in several conditions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The way to place the cup is to place it first empty, suck gently, and apply it quickly, and move it evenly, and do not cease to do this until you see the place reddened and swollen, and the redness of the blood appears; then pierce, and replace the cups, and take care of the body’s condition, for there are those who have thin flesh and open pores: then it is necessary to pierce only once, and to make the wounds wide and a little deep; and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the blood is thick, it is necessary to pierce twice: the first time to refine the way for the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the blood is very thick, it is necessary to pierce a third time; and when we want to draw a small amount of blood, once is enough.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we want a lot of blood, we start again often; and if the blood is thick, pierce deeply, and the purpose is that the heart is pierced suddenly, and for those who have thick and hard skin, and who have narrow pores, you should anoint the places for cupping with opening and dissolving oil: if it is in summer, violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or pumpkin seed oil; and if it is in winter, watercress oil, or lily oil, or chamomile oil, or something similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excess is thick and cold, take amaranth oil, or balsamite oil, or dill oil, and the like.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the one being bled has tender flesh and large pores, there is no need to apply oil, but it should be washed after cupping with rose water, or cold water, or nightshade water, or gourd water, or purslane water, or something similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And he who has much moisture should rise from clary sage water, or myrtle water, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And those who have thick excesses should rise from old wine, or elderflower water, or a decoction of dill or chamomile, or other similar things; and it is not necessary to bleed by cupping before the bath nor in the bath, but rather one or two hours after the bath; and he should not sleep after cupping, and he must be vigilant, both when he is to be cupped and when he has been cupped.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And be mindful if the person being bled has a choleric disposition, and if the blood is too sharp and inflamed; then he must take cool things, such as pomegranates, endives, lettuce with sage, and similar items; also consume young chickens, castrated meat, and moist foods.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And for someone with a cold complexion, he should take honey syrup and medium-aged fragrant wine, which is between old and new, eat little, and consume young chickens and small birds and pigeons; on the day he will be cupped, he should drink more than eat; and it is necessary to give some people theriac or nutmeg before or after cupping, to strengthen the principal organs; the blood should be thinned, but those who are warm should not drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The cups that are placed without piercing are those that are applied to the liver, spleen, gouty joints, the stomach, and the loins, and the hip, because these areas do not tolerate piercing, and are only used to draw blood from one area to another, as in placing them on the breasts when the nose bleeds; to remove the viscosity that is in the organ, as we place cups on the stomach and the belly to reduce swelling; and to remove pain when there is obstruction or stones, as it removes obstruction or can dislodge a stone from its place; it also works similarly when applied to the liver and spleen if there is retained wind, and these cups are administered empty solely for suction; sometimes they are administered with fire, and other times filled with warm water, as in cases of pleurisy, and in such a way that the cup is filled with warm water alone or with water in which suitable herbs have been cooked.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the cup administered with fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	It should be two fingers wide and half a palm deep, with a small hole on the side near the middle, as if to fit a needle, and it should be made of brass, smooth on the front so that it does not hurt the patient when placed on the body; in the middle, it should have a transverse rod of brass or iron, for holding a lit candle, with cups both large and small according to the diseases and the age of the patients; for children’s cups are different from those for the elderly, and for thin people compared to fat ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And you should place this cup on the body as follows: take a wax candle or a lighted cloth, and place it in the center of the cup across the rod in the middle of the cup, so that the flame is at the bottom of the cup, so it does not burn the patient; then place it on the body, and keep your fingers on the hole we mentioned, so that when you wish, the vapor escapes, and the cup is removed; then you take the cloth as before, and repeat often, if needed.
