En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the case of the cup administered for pleurisy, with water, it has no rod or hole, and it is only applied when it is full of water, and is placed directly on the area; and this is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Leeches are only administered in areas where cups cannot be applied due to their smallness, such as lips and gums, and similar locations; and in places lacking flesh, like fingers or nose, and others similar. The procedure for using them is as follows: when you find leeches in clean fresh waters without rot, take them and place them in fresh water for a night until they are clean and have nothing in their stomachs. Then perform bleeding by vein and cupping; rub the area until it is red, and place the leeches on it. When they are full and fall off, if it is a location where a cup can be applied, place it there, as it is highly beneficial afterward.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If this does not work, wash the area with vinegar, then very well with water, then squeeze it; and if the place bleeds too much after the leeches are removed, soak a linen cloth in cold water, and place it on until the blood stops; and if the blood increases, apply powdered vitriol, or gall, and similar things, until it stops; or place peeled fava beans on the area, and leave them until they stick to the place, which will stop it at once; and if you need more, apply other leeches.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the leeches do not attach, rub the area with fresh blood, or prick it with a needle until blood comes out, and then put them on, and as soon as they sense the blood, they will stick; and when you want them to fall off, sprinkle a little powdered aloe and salt, or ashes, on them, and they will fall immediately.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it is a guide to the restoration of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Know, dear son, that foolish doctors avoid this chapter, for they have never seen any of the ancient books, nor read a letter of them; and for this reason, knowledge is rare in our land, for I have never found anyone knowledgeable; and I know nothing of it except through the knowledge of ancient books, in which I have studied so much that I have extracted the science from them, both through experiment and through the habit of my life; and I have already described to you in this chapter what is contained, and I have summarized it at the end, and I have shown clearly the forms of the instruments used, as I have done in the two preceding chapters.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Thus, it is fitting that we say in the prologue of this book the summaries of the word and the chapters where the wise man places his understanding and remains focused on the truth, so that those who are experienced may know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when a fracture, dislocation, twist, or break happens to someone, it is necessary that you hasten to bleed the patient on both sides, unless something prevents it, such as weakness of the body, or if the person is a child or an elderly person; or if the weather is not very hot, or too cold; and they should eat cold foods, namely cold broths, and the meat of birds and goat, and drink no wine, nor eat any fatty meats, and not fill themselves too much with foods that fill the veins with blood, lest you fear a hot abscess or spreading of matter into the limb; thus, the patient should return to their previous diet that they had used.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to heal, it is necessary to nourish the patient with foods that produce substantial nourishment, containing viscosity, such as wheat cooked in water, rice, heads, and feet, and cow stomach, and eggs, and fresh fish, and rich wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For with such nourishment the fracture mends more and faster.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that the broken bones of the old and the decrepit cannot heal or join well according to their nature due to the dryness of the limbs, nor those that are too soft, such as the bones of small children; but no matter, reinforce the broken bone with a thick tendon that will adhere and join the limb together until it strengthens as it was before; and do not deprive it of its work, and therefore it must be nourished with substantial foods, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are varied in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different from the fracture of the chest or of the leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all the types of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is a fracture that goes in an arch, and another that is sharp, like the cut of a pen for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And there is a fracture with a wound, and a fracture with a small crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	Each method has its own tool and its own proper instrument in the restoration, as memory serves in its place; and the bone fracture is known by the fact that the place is twisted, and it clearly appears from the outside, and sounds when pressed by the hand; and when there is no twisting nor sound upon touching, and the patient does not feel great pain, there is no fracture; but it may well have a twist, a crack, or a small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	It is not necessary to move it by hand, but apply the medicines that follow here, and then gently bind it right away.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And know that a fracture that is displaced, with the two parts disjointed, must be set in alignment immediately, before any swelling arises; and if swelling does occur, leave it for a few days, until the swelling subsides; then set it in alignment as gently and wisely as you can, and know that its restoration is easier than the restoration of one where there are fragments; then bind it, as will be explained below.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if the bone has broken pieces, stretch it from both sides, if it’s a hand or foot, or with your hand if it’s a small limb, or with two cords, or with a cord and your hand; and set the limb according to its natural shape, so that when the parts of the broken limb are separated, bring all the segments back to their places as best you can, and take care that your work does not cause the patient any injury or pain; and join the two ends of the bones in the best way.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And feel it well with your hand if it doesn’t seem right to you: then adjust it gently, and don’t bind it too tightly, nor press as do those who cause swelling and contraction in the limb with their work, as we have seen many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the limb is properly set, instruct the patient well not to move it, neither while awake nor asleep, nor while turning, nor in any other way; and make sure that the limb is so stabilized that it feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when it feels any pain, it is not set correctly, and it must be placed in such a position that it feels no pain; and be careful to set it straight, so that no twisting occurs when it is restored; and the nature of the broken limb is as I have described to you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken limbs vary in size, in length, and in shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For there are small members, such as arms, fingers, and similar: they must be wrapped in soft, fine linen cloths; and those that are large, like the thigh and leg, must be wrapped with a wide and firm bandage, as the wide band covers the whole large limb and compresses it evenly on all sides, so that there is no fault in the binding. Then wrap around it light layers of wool, three or four times according to the limb, and press your hand gently on the whole bandage, then go above the fracture and press less firmly, so that the binding can extend slightly beyond the fracture. Gradually soften the band, so that you cover a large portion of the healthy area; then take another band, and wrap it again over the fractured area. Then return to the part below the fracture and bind it moderately—not too tight nor too loose, as we said for the first banding above. Then place between the bands linen or cloth padding, so that it is all even, then cover everything with a bandage; and then place your well-made splints on top, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is swelling or an abscess, apply something to soothe the hot abscess, which reduces the swelling, and leave it on for several days; then bind with splints, and let them be half the width of a wide cane, carefully smoothed, or made of wood for cleaving, or of palm branches, and shaped as follows:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	but the splint applied over the fracture must be a bit thicker and wider than the others; and it should be as long as necessary according to the limb’s size or length; then bind over the splints as you did with the first layer, then bind above with a proper thread, as in the first layer over the fracture; tighter at the top, gradually looser; and the threads should be medium, neither too thick nor too thin, and made of soft linen; for if the threads are thick, as I have seen in the work of fools who use twisted linen cords for their bindings, that is a great error, for the binding cannot be even if it is too thick, and there should not be less than two fingers’ space between each splint.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is injured by the ends of the splints after binding in uninjured areas, place lint or teased wool underneath them so they are not hurt.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is along with the fracture, and the skin is broken, I will describe the treatment below.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not necessary to bind with splints all broken limbs on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the limb is large, splints do not need to be applied until after five or seven days, or more depending on your caution about the onset of hot abscess; and here is the method of the ancient plasters for restoring fractures, dislocations, and twisting: take flour that clings to the walls of the mill, and mix it with plenty of egg, and apply this mixture, neither too thin nor too thick, and use it, and this is the common type of plaster that restores fractures in various situations, especially for women and small children, for it is neither too hot nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana V З.; alechil VIIII З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another kind of plaster for restoring fractures, dislocations, and twisting: take 3 drams each of abaris, ladanum, enula, asafoetida, Arabic gum, and mugwort; 5 drams each of myrrh and aloes; 9 drams of alchil; and make them into powder, and mix with plenty of egg; if the person’s complexion is warm, use this plaster, for it is of good composition and quickly restores broken bones, and is beneficial to many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another kind of plaster that is good for twisting: take 10 drams each of mugwort and marshmallow; 9 drams each of myrrh and aloes; 6 drams of acacia; 10 drams of Armenian bole, and grind well, and mix with water or plenty of egg, and apply it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another kind of plaster for joints and bones displaced from their positions, and it soothes the arising pain, and cuts the bruising from the bone and the fracture: take new wool, soak it in vinegar and boiled oil, and apply to the area.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	This plaster does not restore, but it is good for soothing a hot abscess and properly removes the pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another kind of plaster that restores broken bones: take dried fig leaves, and leaves of ground poppy, and grind together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another kind of plaster for restoring bone fractures and to reduce the remaining swelling.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take root of marshmallow, chamomile, violet flowers, vetch flour, one part of each; and grind, and mix with wine, and if the limb is inflamed, mix it with moist coriander water, or plain water, and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another kind of plaster, stronger than the first, when hard abscess arises during the restoration of the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take marshmallow roots, linseed, pomegranate rind, melilot, and mullein, and violet and chamomile flowers, one part of each; grind, and mix with salt water, or plain water, or with wine, depending on the heat of the limb, and its relaxation.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates says in his book that for restoring a broken limb, only apply a cerate made of wax and oil, and nothing else, and he says it should be neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And Galen suggests that to restore a broken limb, one should apply dry things, somewhat warm, like myrrh, aloes, incense, and similar items, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another kind of plaster for wounds and pain: take mugwort and cut human hair, or bird feathers, and marshmallow, and salt in equal measure, grind them, make a plaster and apply it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors. Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;  puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then, loosen it a little afterwards, and check if the patient feels no pain, and the bone has not moved from its place; if so, do not untie it for several days. And if pain, itching, unrest, or swelling occurs at the site, quickly loosen it, remove the plaster immediately; take a light cloth and a damp sea sponge, plunge it in water, and cleanse the area until the itching stops and the pain is soothed. Then let the limb rest for an hour, then put dry wool on it, moistened with water or rose oil, and bind it for one night, until you are sure there is no hot abscess. And let the inflammation of the limb subside, and the pain be removed, then begin the gentle binding again, with a little plaster, but do not bind it as tightly as before; and continue gently until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the hot abscess, redness, pain, and swelling have entirely gone, and you need a poultice and binding, then start again, just as you did the first time, evenly.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	And if none of the issues we have mentioned arise in the limb, then it should not be unbound until after three, four, five, seven days, or even sometimes left for twenty days, depending on what is observed, until the fracture sets and the flesh draws near to cover it. Then tighten it more than before and enrich the patient’s food, as I mentioned above. If you see the area drying more than necessary, know that nourishment cannot reach it; then moisten it with lukewarm water every time you unbind it, which should be every third day, and loosen the band a little. By this procedure, nourishment will reach the limb, quickly improving what the foolish doctors worsen by setting the limb incorrectly; that is harmful and a dangerous practice, and I see nothing else to do but to let it heal and to treat it properly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	Of the different types of fractures
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	There are many types of fractures, and different shapes, and the causes are distinct; for there are fractures caused by the blow of a sword, and the blade removes all the bone down to the tissue beneath the bone, as an axe does to wood; and for this reason, this type of fracture is called "splitting."
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	Or the sword cuts the bone from above without piercing it, and this type of fracture is called "simple"; and the wound from these two fractures can be large or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is an embedded blow, or a split from a blow with a stone, or from falling onto a stone, or other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a piercing fracture, which reaches down to the tissue beneath the bone, or it is on the bone, and this wound can be either large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And there is a wound that appears on the bone as fine as a hair, and the split is small, and so this fracture is called "capillary"; and there is also the wound made by a blow from a stone, or by a fall, or something similar, which forces a piece of the bone downward, and the area is dented as when a hammer strikes a cauldron; so the stone penetrates within.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And this happens more to those who have soft bones in the head, such as a child's head; and with all these types of fractures, small pieces are detached as splinters; and I will speak about it in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we recognize all types of fractures by the depression upon them, by probing with tents, and by the corrupted flesh above.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The capillary appearance is known by the fact that when the bone is uncovered, and rubbed above, the fracture appears black.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of the fracture, take note of the patient's symptoms, and if you see any bad symptoms, such as vomiting of bile, loss of understanding, convulsions, fainting, high fever, and the eyes protruding and reddening, and other similar signs in various conditions, then healing is doubtful.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you see no frightening symptoms, and you hope for healing, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the wounded person first comes to you, and it is in winter, it is necessary to remove the bone before the fourteenth day at the latest if you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is summer, then hasten to remove the bone before the seventh day, before the tissue beneath the bone becomes corrupted, and the symptoms we have mentioned appear.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the fracture of the bone reaches to the tissue that covers the brain, then it is necessary to cut the fractured part like this: you take the head of the wounded patient, uncover the bone in every way you can, and around the shape of the wound as gently as you can, and if bleeding occurs while uncovering the bone, or there is a hot abscess, assist it as necessary, and fill the area with cloths soaked in rose oil; and let the wound rest until the hot abscess is calmed, and you are assured there is no bleeding; then begin to remove around the bone, and this is done according to two methods of work: the first method is that you cut narrowly in front, and this is the form:
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then add another cut larger than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second method is that you have a number of different cuts, some narrow and others wide, and pointed, and made of steel; and work lightly, so as not to injure the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is strong and hard, it is necessary to pierce it around, before applying cuts with drills, not so deep that they go through the bone of the head, and the tip should have a border or ring above it, to prevent the point from going through the bone; and you need to have several, so that each one corresponds to the thickness of the bone, so that you have drills for every head; and this is the form of the three types of drills:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The method for drilling around the fractured bone is to place a drill on the bone, and turn it with your fingers until you know that the bone is pierced; then place the drill a little further away, and do this all around, then cut with an incisor the thickness of the bone between the holes, and do this as delicately as you can, and lightly, as we have said, until you extract the bone by hand, or with one of the instruments you have, such as forceps or pincers; and take care not to touch the brain or the membrane.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have pierced the bone and extracted it, it is necessary to scrape the remainder of the bone with another instrument similar to an incisor, but it must be thinner and more delicate than the other incisor; and if any small bones or fragments remain, remove them gently with one of the instruments; then treat the wound with tents and ointments as we have described.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other method of work is that which Galen described, which is safer; he greatly praised it, and these are his words.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	First, it is necessary to uncover a part of the bone, where the fracture is clearly visible, so that when you have uncovered this part, you will place the head of this lenticular-shaped incisor beneath it, of which this is the form:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And it does not cut from one side, and has sharp edges on both sides, so that the cutting edge is toward the bone; then strike lightly with a small mallet, so that you gently cut the bone all around, and be very careful of the tissue beneath; if it is adhering to the bone, remove it gently, for it can be removed without harm and without fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone fracture does not pierce through to the tissue, and the bone is only cut on the surface, and there are small pieces, it is necessary to smooth out this roughness, and remove the splinters with a delicate rasp, of which you should have various sizes, to be used in each place as best fits the work and the shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	First, use large rasps, and then finer ones, and do not stop until it is well done.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other capillary cuts and subtle fractures, you must provide treatment according to its positioning; and this is not something unknown to one who has studied this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And if the membrane is exposed, it is necessary to take a linen cloth, according to the size of the wound, moisten it with rose oil, and place it on the wound; then take another cloth, folded in two or three, moisten it with wine and rose oil, and place it on the first cloth; do this as gently as you can, so as not to harm the membrane, then apply another binding over it, but do not tie it tighter than is necessary to keep the wound covered; leave it thus for a day or two, until the hot abscess has calmed, then untie it, and apply medicines such as lily roots, bean flour, frankincense powder, aristolochia, and similar substances; make a powder from these things, and put it on the wound, and apply gentle cleansing medicines without biting action; and ensure the wound is always clean, not leaving ointment on it, nor allowing dirt to accumulate, for when dirt collects on the tissue of the brain, it corrupts and rots it, causing great harm to the patient; for when something biting is placed on the membrane, it irritates from above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take care, then, that if any bad symptoms appear in the patient, as we have mentioned, it is indeed dangerous.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if darkness appears there only because of the medicine applied, which has such a property, it is necessary to take one part honey, and three parts rose oil, and soak a cloth in it, and place it on the membrane; then treat it with the necessary treatments until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that sometimes the two upper parts of the nose are broken, or just one by itself, for these are two bones; the lower one is cartilaginous and does not break, it only swells or twists, and then heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two parts is broken, you must put your little finger in the nostril, and align the fracture inside with your index finger and thumb on the outside, until the nose returns to its natural shape; and do this gently, taking care that the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the fracture is on the upper part of the nose, and the finger cannot reach the place, it is necessary to set it right at the tip of a somewhat thick stick.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the fracture is in two parts, do the same, and hurry to restore it on the first day, if you can; if not, after the seventh or tenth day, when the hot swelling is reduced, then place linen cloth tents at the top of the nose if the fracture is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or place another on the other side if the fracture is there; and the tents should be thick enough to fill the nasal passages.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And some restorers say to moisten the tents with butter and change them every day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	It does not seem right to me, but rather they should be moistened with a mixture of egg white and millstone powder; then leave the tent until the bone is firm and the cartilage hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes one places goose feathers in the nose instead of tents, with a soft cloth around, and the fracture holds, and the patient breathes through it; so do whichever you wish.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if a hot swelling comes to the nose while you are working on it, place wax or cotton soaked in rose oil, or in a bit of diacolon.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if hot swelling does not appear, then place a plaster on the outside, made of sesame flour and incense powder, mixed with egg white, then put light tow on top, and do not bind the nose; and if the fracture of the nose is small, and it is broken into small pieces, extract them with suitable instruments, then stitch the wound and treat it with things that promote flesh and healing, like appropriate plasters and ointments; and if there is no wound inside the nose, treat it with tents and place lead sheets in it until it is healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	On the fracture of the jaw
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jaw is broken below and there is no outer wound, and the fracture is only on the outside, not broken in two, just dented inside, it is easily recognized.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	If the fracture is on the right side, place your index finger in the patient’s mouth; and if the fracture is on the left jaw, place your index finger of the right hand in, gently push the fracture inward, align it from outside with the other hand, and set it straight.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the jaw is separated in two, you must provide extension from two sides until it is even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if there is movement of the teeth or fracture, bind them with a thread of gold, silver, or silk, then apply wax on the broken jaw, and place a double cloth on it; and place on the cloth a large well-made splint, or a piece of smooth leather, long and wide according to the jaw, and tie it as tightly as possible, and instruct the patient to rest and eat light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	And if you see the shape changing, untie it on the third day, then readjust what has changed; apply a plaster made of mill powder with egg white or sesame flour, after removing the wax; and apply light wool on the plaster, and if the plaster sticks and the condition of the patient doesn’t change, leave it until it heals; often it heals within three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if a hot abscess appears, apply what we have mentioned many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is both a fracture and a wound, check if any bone fragment is removed; carefully remove it with suitable instruments.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, enlarge it with a flame as needed.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces, and none remain, sew up the wound if it is large, and apply a suitable plaster on it to generate flesh, until it heals.
de la forcele	Regarding the clavicle
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The clavicle often breaks at the front, near the shoulder, and the fracture occurs in three ways: either it is broken and separated in two, and there are pieces, and this is the easiest to repair; or there is a fracture with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparence ne chevement.	And the procedure is, when the fracture is without a wound, that you have two assistants, one holding the support for the broken clavicle, and the other extending the neck towards the area; then set the fracture with your fingers so that the form is as it should be, with no irregularity or protrusion.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need more extension, place a round ball of cloth or wool under the patient's shoulder, as thick as necessary; and stretch and lift the clavicle, pressing the ball with your hand so that you align the fracture as needed.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot draw the end of the clavicle outward because it is too deep, the patient should lie often on his back, placing a medium pillow under the shoulder, while the assistant pushes the shoulder downward until the clavicle bone is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	Then align the fracture with your fingers, and if you find it shattered, you must cut it open; gently extract the pieces, and if the bone cannot be joined due to any prominence, cut it with one of the incisors you have; but place this instrument under the clavicle to protect the tissue.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	It resembles a spoon and is not sharp, and should be as wide as needed according to the size of the bone and the strength of the work; it has two ends, as you see, one wide and the other narrow, according to the nature of the wound you made when you extracted the bone fragments; and when you are certain there is no hot abscess, sew the wound, and if the fracture is small or you suspect a hot abscess, fill the wound with cloths and tents as needed.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if a hot abscess appears there, soak a cloth in rose oil, garlic, and wine, and apply it.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	The treatment for a bone fracture without wounds or cuts is as follows: apply a poultice made of mill dust and egg white to the bone, then place a light layer of tow (soft fibers) over it. If necessary, place a wedge under the armpit for support. Next, take a very long bandage about a palm wide, and place a double layer of cloth over the tow and the poultice. Then take a thin splint three fingers wide and long enough, wrap the bandage around it so that the ends of the bandage hang down, and place the splint over the fracture. Wrap the bandage over the shoulder and under both the healthy and injured armpits, securing it from each side. When the binding holds the fracture in place securely and the splint remains steady over the broken bone, check it daily. When the binding loosens, retighten it. The patient should lie on their back, and when they sleep, place a small pillow under the armpit to elevate and support the injury, which will relieve the strain on the fracture by aligning the shoulder. Secure the arm to the neck and do not untie it unless complications arise for twenty days. Then, if necessary, reapply the poultice, tighten the bandage, and continue until the bone is healed. Full healing typically takes about twenty-eight days, though some may heal faster.
de la brisure de l’espaule	Regarding the fracture of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	Sometimes, the shoulder is fractured in a wide area or in the middle, and this may not be evident except by touch. First, set it according to the shape of the fracture, restoring it as close to its natural form as possible in every way you can. Then apply mill dust mixed with egg white to the area, followed by a light layer of tow (soft fibers) and a double-folded cloth. Place a wide, thin splint over the area, slightly broader than the shoulder. If the splint does not sit evenly at any point, fill the uneven areas with flax tow so that the splint is even. Then secure it firmly with a wide bandage so that the splint does not shift from its position, and check the binding each day. Whenever it loosens, tighten it, and ensure the splint remains aligned if it has shifted. The patient should lie on their side. The shoulder will generally heal in twenty to twenty-five days. Once this period is complete, you may remove the binding. Rest assured, as the bone will not easily shift out of place after healing.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of bone protrudes and presses below the heart, then cut it open and remove it, and do as we have said regarding the clavicle fracture to ease a hot abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	Regarding the fracture of the chest
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The chest is sometimes broken in the middle, though this is rare; it more often breaks on the outside.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, it shifts downward, and the patient feels great pain, shortness of breath, and coughs, and may even vomit blood, and the unevenness of the broken bone is apparent and can be felt easily.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	The treatment is for the patient to lie often on his back with a cushion between the shoulders, then press the shoulders and bring together the ribs on both sides with your hands, making every effort to align the bone so that its shape is as it should be; then apply plasters and stuffings above a fine splint made of willow or other light wood, wrap it in a cloth, and tie it securely over the broken bone so it does not move; wrap the binding evenly around the back, and tighten it moderately, adjusting the bandage every hour, and if it loosens, tighten it; and if it needs to be loosened due to corrosion, itching, pain, or abscess at the location, act quickly, loosen it, scrape the plaster, and apply any necessary treatments; then replace the plaster and tighten it until it heals.
de la brisure des costes	Regarding the fracture of the ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Know that rib fractures only occur in thick parts near the back and at the inner end, and they only bend because they are flexible; this can be easily detected by feeling with the fingers.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the treatment is to set the fracture straight, as needed.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	Then apply a plaster and secure it with a splint, if necessary.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the rib fracture is inward, the patient feels very sharp pain, like pleurisy, because the bone pierces the pleura; he has difficulty breathing, coughs, and vomits a large amount of blood, which is very dangerous, and the ancients devised various remedies for it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And there are some who say he should be given foods that swell the belly to push the fracture outward.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do this, to avoid causing a hot abscess, unless one has already developed.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has developed, then treat it.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And some of them say that one should place cups on the area to draw out strongly, and this seems reasonable; however, there is concern that the cups might draw impurities to the area due to its weakened state.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And some of them say one should cover the area with wool soaked in hot oil, and place tents between the ribs to apply even pressure around, then treat with pleurisy remedies, diet, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot endure due to the bone piercing the pleura, and there is danger to the patient, then it is necessary to cut open the area of the broken rib and place an instrument underneath to protect the tissue; then the bone must be trimmed and gently pulled, and then sew the two sides of the wound if it is large, and treat it with plasters until it heals.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if a hot abscess appears, apply cloths soaked in rose oil on the area; and treat the area as needed for an abscess, and have him lie often on the side he should, until it heals.
de la brisure dou col	Regarding the fracture of the neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Sometimes a fracture occurs in the bones of the neck, and rarely do they bend; and likewise in the spinal column.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to someone, and you want to know if he will recover or not, check if you see his hands softened, swollen, and numb, and he cannot move or extend them, and when you prick them with a needle, he does not feel it.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that this is usually fatal, but if he can move them and feels well when they are squeezed or pricked, know that the bone joint is intact, and the patient will be healed if treated.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if similar symptoms appear in the spine, and you wish to know if he will recover, observe if his feet have become soft and if the symptoms present are like those in the hands, and if there is involuntary passage of gas and stools while lying on his back; if, when lying on his stomach, involuntary stool occurs.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when he is on his back and tries to sit up, he cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	Know that this condition is usually fatal, so do not attempt to treat it.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if these symptoms do not appear, the condition is less serious.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	The treatment is to observe if there is a hot abscess. If there is, apply rose oil or egg yolk oil to the spine until the area is soothed; then apply a plaster that is comforting and drying, tie it in place, and instruct the patient to rest. He should not sleep on the side where he feels pain until he is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if any bone becomes dislodged, it is necessary to cut open the area, remove the bone, and then join the two edges of the wound, if it is large, with a suture. Then treat the wound with healing ointments that generate new flesh until it is healed. If the head of the bone is broken—what is called the “head of the tail”—insert the thumb of your left hand and align it as best as you can with your other hand, then apply a plaster and splint, if needed; then tighten the splint, and if there is any loose bone, cut open the area, remove it, and treat the wound until it is fully healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	Regarding the fracture of the hip bone
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	It is rare for the hip bone to break, and if it does, it usually occurs only as a slight chipping at the top. The fracture is long and inclines inward, causing pain, sharp discomfort, and swelling at the break.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	The treatment is to place your hand on the affected area and feel the break, determining its shape. If the fracture is only at the top, align it to its natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	If the fracture is long or inclines inward, have the patient lie on his stomach until the treatment is ready.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	Once it is set in place, apply a plaster, then place a wooden or leather splint over it and secure the break so it does not move. Pack the area below the ribs to ensure the alignment.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	Instruct the patient to sleep on his healthy side or on his back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if a hot abscess forms, do not touch it until it subsides; then apply the treatments previously mentioned, and continue with the restoration, securing it as needed if there are no other complications. This is the procedure.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	Regarding the fracture of the “adjutoire” (the bone between the shoulder blade and the upper arm)
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The “adjutoire” is the bone between the elbow and the head of the shoulder, and if it is fractured, it can be set in one of two ways. The first way is to take a piece of wood of moderate thickness, shaped as follows:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	Tie two cords to each end of the wood and hang it up; then seat the patient on a chair, place his broken arm over the wood, up to the armpit, and place a curved piece of wood in between. Then hang a weight or have the assistants stretch it downward; the doctor then aligns the break with his hands until it is properly set.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	The second method is to lay the patient on his side, tie his hand to his neck, then instruct two assistants: one should hold above the fracture with his hands, and the other should hold below it with a band, with each extending their side.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	If you wish to increase the extension, tie a band above and below the fracture, and each assistant should stretch his side.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	If the fracture is near the head of the shoulder, place a band under the armpit and another near the elbow, below the fracture. Similarly, if it is closer to the elbow, place a light band carefully until the break is properly aligned at the shoulder and elbow. Then secure the fracture as needed, provided no hot abscess develops.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if hot swelling appears there, do not bind it for seven days, and place moistened wool with vinegar and rose oil on it until the hot swelling is calmed; then bind it, and the way to bind it is to place the plaster over the fracture, then set the arm on the support, placing your hand on the shoulder or chest; put on the cloth, and bind it onto the support and the arm, so that the arm serves as a splint, unless something prevents you, or if the bone is not displaced.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you fear that the bone may move, use splints, and place over the fracture a splint wider and stronger than the others, with a space of one finger's width between each splint, and each splint should be large enough to extend three fingers' width beyond the fracture on each side; then bind over the splints, as I said at the beginning of the chapter on fractures, tighter and with less spacing.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	And if you see the positioning of the splints and the binding, as we have said, when you restore the broken limb, and you fear a hot swelling, leave it unbound until the seventh day, as we have said; then check the binding every three days, so that no itching or swelling appears there, or so that nourishment can reach the limb, as it would be too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	Adjust it, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	And if none of these incidents appear, do not loosen it except after three days or more, and let the patient sleep on their back, with their hands on their stomach; place under the support a cushion evenly filled with wool, and check every hour of the day or night that the form of the broken limb does not move, or that the binding is not loosened; adjust it by medical means, and give the patient food as we have prescribed before, so that at first the food is light; and when they start to recover, let it be substantial.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	And it is customary that the support and the leg should be rebandaged in forty days altogether; and then it should be unbound and given baths and medicinal ointments to strengthen the area.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the constriction is severe and swollen, it should remain bound for fifty days or two months.
de la brisure du bras	On fractures of the arm
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of two bones, called the two "fosciles," of which one is small, and it is the one that follows the thumb; and the other is large, and it is the one underneath, toward the little finger; sometimes only the large "foscile" is broken, or the small one, and sometimes both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the small "foscile" is broken, the restoration is easy, as is the healing; but when the large one is broken, the healing is difficult, and more serious than when both are broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it is only the small "foscile" that is broken, then it must be slightly extended and set evenly.
