Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	And if it is the large "foscile," it must be bound more tightly; extend it on a cushion, and hold the thumb of the hand higher than the others, and the little finger lower than the other fingers, and let the patient cross themselves, and place a cushion in front of them higher, so that the patient does not endure any strain; then the assistant extends their arm underneath to the hand or to a binding, and another assistant on the other above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then the physician sets it evenly, according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if there are pieces in the fracture, place each one in its place, and if there is one displaced that pains the heart, and you cannot restore it to its place, then cut open and remove it, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if there is a wound with the fracture, I have spoken of it in the separate chapter; take the necessary care.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And if at the start of the restoration hot swelling appears, apply a cloth of cerate made of rose oil and white wax, not too hard or too soft; and bind the cloth over it delicately, until the hot swelling is calmed.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	Then remove the wax dressing and apply a poultice made from mill dust mixed with egg white. Next, place the splints, with the splint over the fracture area being stronger and slightly wider than the others. There should be six splints on the arm in various positions, whether the fracture is in one bone or in both. Apply greater tightness over the fracture itself and progressively less tightness moving away from it, as I described at the beginning of this chapter. The cloths covering the fracture should be soft and moist, not hard or rough. Use linen threads to secure the bindings, neither too thick nor too thin, as previously noted.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And check the limb and the binding after some days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if any bad incident affects the limb, such as itching that appears on the limb, pour warm water over the limb until the itching is calmed; and let the limb rest without tight binding.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	Then reapply the binding, and if the bandage is loose and the bone displaced, or similar, adjust it.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And take care that if nourishment cannot reach the limb because it is too tight, you must loosen it a bit, and leave it like that for a few days so that nourishment flows there, and then tighten it again.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these issues occur to the patient, do not loosen it for twenty days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	Or around that time, then hang their hands around their neck, and make sure they keep it even, and avoid movement and strain, and sleep on their back; and know that this fracture heals in thirty or thirty-five days, or possibly in twenty days, depending on the constitution and strength of the individual.
de la brisure de la main	On fractures of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that fractures rarely happen on the back of the hand or at the joints of the fingers, and often it is only sprains that occur.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	And when the palm of the hand is fractured or sprained, the patient must sit cross-legged, sitting upright and evenly before him; then place his hand on the extended cloth, and the assistant stretches the fractured bones, and the physician sets them evenly, so that they are well joined; apply the plaster and wadding, if no swelling appears, then place a splint according to the area’s size, and wrap it in a linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the fracture is on the inner part, near the middle of the palm, make a ball of cloths, and instruct the patient to grip it with his fractured palm; then bind it with a long cloth, and the splint should be smooth and as large as the palm, and bind it as required.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is on the outside, you must place a splint on top and another beneath the palm, so that the hand is open and straight; then bind it all around the hand, and secure the binding between the fingers.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the fracture occurs at one of the finger joints, if it is the thumb, set it evenly as required; bind it along with the palm, and if you wish, place a small straight splint to keep the fracture lifted and immobile; and if the fracture is on another finger, like the index or one of the others, set it evenly, and bind it to the healthy finger next to it; or bind them all in a single hold, which is often effective, or place a splint as with the thumb; and take care in the restoration and management of any hot swelling, and treat it as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	On fractures of the thigh
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	The thigh bone is often fractured, and it is evident when it turns forward or backward; and the treatment is to bind one band above the fracture and another below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient lies on their back, then each assistant stretches their band evenly on their side; and this is when the fracture is in the middle of the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the fracture is near the root of the thigh, one band should be toward the hip and the other band below the fracture.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And also if it is near the knee, then let the band be near the knee, and let the extension be downward; then the physician sets the bone evenly with his two hands, until it is in its natural shape, then applies the plaster and binds it, if no hot swelling appears.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is hot swelling, let it calm before returning to your work and care; the binding is done in this way.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	You must wrap a firm bandage, doubled two or three times, over the fracture to absorb any excess discharge. Then turn the leg so that the heel is positioned at the base of the buttock, and place a long thread between the thigh and the leg, just below the knee, with the ends of the thread coming out above. Then wind the bandage up over the leg and the thigh, place splints over the fracture, and position one splint over the shin bone. Fill the empty space between the leg and the thigh with soft cloths to ensure an even pressure; then begin to bind it tightly with three or four turns around the fracture, loosening the tension as you move upward from the fracture. Next, focus on the two ends of the thread that you placed between the leg and thigh, and use them to secure the three uppermost splints; then bring the thread down to its starting point at the foot, keeping it taut so the splints stay in place. Finally, leave it as is, as long as no abscess, swelling, or other complication appears.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if it happens, untie it, and adjust what comes as we have often said; and if there are pieces of bone pressing, it is necessary to remove them if one can; and if one cannot, it is necessary to split the place and draw out fire; and treat it as we have said, until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And sometimes the thigh is broken so that splints are put there, as in the arm and the forearm; nevertheless, in the restoration done in this way, the patient does not limp.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the thigh is restored in fifty days, or a little less or a little more, according to the differences in constitutions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	Of the hollow of the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	Know that in the hollow of the knee, breaks rarely happen, but it bends often.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, it is only a split or a hole, and it happens with a wound or without a wound, and one can feel this well.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is to place what is round against its joints until they are brought together as much as possible; then apply the plaster, and place a round splint if needed, and bind it as required, then review all the instructions we have given for other breaks, like warm swelling and similar; apply to each condition what is needed until it is healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	Of the break of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	Know that in the leg there are two bones, of which one is rightly called "mustel," and the other is called "foscile"; and a break occurs just as it does in the arm, and therefore the restoration is just like that of the arm, and the procedure is the same. And if the two bones are broken together, the leg turns in all directions.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the thin bone is broken, it turns forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the large bone is broken, one feels great pain, and it is clearly seen; and it turns downward.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	Then administer traction, and set it evenly, and bind the splints equally; but nevertheless, if the break is severe, and there are many pieces, the extension must be lighter and more gentle; and adjust it according to your skill.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed all your work, take two pieces of wood shaved to fit the leg on either side, and they should be as long as the leg from the knee down; then wrap a bandage in two places, above and below, and tie it in the middle as well, and then the leg will not incline to the right or left, and this is good; and some apply a rod along the length of the leg, and it is of wood, and place the leg on it to prevent movement, and do this particularly in a break with a wound; move the leg each day to see if there is warm swelling or any other condition; treat it until it is healed.
de la brisure des os dou piet	Of the break of the bones of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle there is rarely a break, but sometimes there is a break in the bones of the foot, and little in the toes, and there is usually only a crack in several places.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if there is a break in the bones of the foot, and you see these bones overlapping, then have the patient put his foot on the ground as if he wanted to walk, and then put your foot on his where the bones are raised, then press until they return to their places; then apply the plaster and padding on top, and place a small board with two flat edges under the arch of the foot, then bind it to the foot appropriately, after you have wrapped cloths around and whatever else you need.
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And after three or four days have passed, untie the binding, for you will find the bones aligned, whether broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if any of the toes are broken, restore them as we have said for the fingers of the hand; then place a splint on the broken toe along its length, and it should be a bit wider, then place under the foot that board I mentioned, and bind it appropriately; and if there are two or three, or more, broken, then place a splint on each toe according to its size, wrapped in a linen cloth, and bind the board under the foot; and it should be positioned on the end of the board beyond the arch of the foot, so that it holds well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And it is necessary that you do not forget the other things I have said for other breaks, as we have mentioned; and address each condition as is necessary.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	Of the break of the wrist bone
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bone of a woman’s pelvis is fractured, have her sit with her legs apart, then lean her back toward her spine and ensure she is supported from behind. Then fill the cavity of the affected area with cotton, making it as thick as a finger. Afterward, have the woman stand up, gently raising her back little by little, and in doing so, the cotton will move upward, pushing the bone back into place along with the cotton. When she needs to urinate, remove the cotton, and after she has urinated, replace it. Continue this process for about seven days, and the fracture will be restored. If you wish, take a sheep’s bladder, tie a tube to its opening, and insert the entire bladder into the cavity; then blow forcefully through the tube until the bladder inflates within. This inflation will realign the fracture. Then fill the cavity with cotton and leave it in place for several days until it is fully healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	And when the wrist bone of the man or woman is broken, restore it as we have said for the hip bone; and these breaks are not hidden from one who dedicates study and practice to it and understands my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For the break in its various forms shows the correct way of restoration: understand it then.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the rod, when it is broken, take a goose neck and insert the rod; then wrap it with cloths around, and leave it three days or thereabouts, and it will heal quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	Of a break with a wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for one who has a break with a wound, especially if it is large, as in the thigh bone or arm or similar, to be bled immediately, as the bleedings we have mentioned confirm.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound heals, cleanse it with vitriol if you have nothing else, then begin to restore the break at that same time, or that day, if no warm swelling appears.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if warm swelling appears, delay the restoration until the ninth day, until the swelling subsides, and do not touch it on the third day or fourth, as you would cause a harmful effect.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is exposed on the uncovered part, you must set it gently with your hands, with slight extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extension is not sufficient for setting by hand, then use this iron instrument, which is seven or eight fingers long, and the width is in proportion to the wound; and for this, the doctor should have three or four, according to need in each case of break; it should be round and somewhat thick, so it does not bend with the compression on the limb in your work, and should be sharp in front, thickening from the middle forward, like this:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	It is called "palainche," so that the curved end is placed on the head of the exposed bone; and press it at once until it returns, and so it is aligned one against the other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the break is fine, and the instrument cannot hold the bone well, then you must cut the bone's head until the instrument can take hold.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot bring the bone back as we said, cut it with a suitable instrument, either a cutter or saw, as best as you can; then scrape what remains on the bone of roughness and small scales.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is set, and the patient feels great pain afterward, know that it is not in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	So ensure it is in its place, then wet a cloth in black styptic wine, especially if it is in summer; and do not put on the wound any wax or other thing with oil, as it could cause rot and infection; then apply splints once you have set the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and cut the covering all around according to the size of the wound, and be careful that the wound is not tightened with the break; for foolish doctors have done this many times, causing death or festering in the patient; and make the binding softer and gentler than for other breaks.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	And if the wound is bad or large, and you fear that bad effects may arise, as we have said, and you find pain in the area, then do not apply splints; instead wrap it with hard cloths around in place of splints, and bind them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see, after one or two days, fluid forming at the wound, remove what you had applied with wine, and apply a healing ointment for wounds, such as tetrapharmacon ointment and similar.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you untie the limb twice a day, morning and evening, until it is joined and healed.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the limb be positioned so that the fluid flows down easily.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if many days pass and it cannot heal but always oozes fluid, know that there are small pieces of bone, for which it is necessary that you probe the wound with a tent and remove all these loose pieces causing this pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula appears in the area, or some other form of corruption, it is necessary for you to treat it, according to what was said in the previous chapter.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when the bone is broken and visible on the limb, such as the bone of the thigh or of the hip, and other similar large bones, do not pull it, for often death results; instead, let it rot until it naturally falls away after twenty or thirty days, then treat the wound if you can; if not, leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	Of blisters that form over the union.
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	Often, after the healing of the fracture, especially when it is near the joint, the appearance of the limb is unsightly; and it may happen that the limb cannot perform its natural functions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Then, if the swelling is fresh, apply styptic medicines such as aloe, incense, myrrh, sarcocolla, acacia, and similar substances. Take some of these or all together, and blend them with styptic wine, egg white, or vinegar; apply them on the swelling with lint, bind it tightly, and do not loosen it for several days; then remove it, and begin anew, until the swelling is gone. Alternatively, you can press a well-shaped lead piece onto it, as lead has the property of removing all swellings from limbs. If the swelling has already hardened like stone and must be removed, then cut above it, splitting the visible excess; or shave it down with a razor until it is removed, and tend to it until it heals.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	Of the limb that is weak after healing.
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the bone fracture is healed, and the limb remains weak and thin, it occurs for many reasons: one is because it was bound too tightly and not as it should have been; or because there was too much binding, preventing nourishment from reaching the limb; or due to too much moistening; or due to too much movement, not at the right time; or because the body has little blood, hence it is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	The treatment is to make the patient eat, and strengthen the body until his blood is increased; give him baths, and provide joy and cheer; then apply a weight to the limb, so that the weight draws nourishment to it, and often moisten it with warm water, so that nourishment flows to the limb, and it returns to its natural form.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	Of the limb twisted after healing.
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limb is twisted after healing, and the broken bone is visible, and the shape of the limb is unsightly, yet it still retains its natural function, do not believe those fools who say that the limb must be broken anew, and many foolish doctors have done this in our land; this work is condemned, and it causes great harm and perhaps death. However, if the swelling and twisting are fresh, it is necessary to moisten them with warm water, or cook softening herbs, like mallow leaves, roots, and melilot, and similar things; prepare a softening plaster, like a well-made diacylon, and take mallow mucilage, mix it with chicken fat or sesame oil, and apply a plaster. Alternatively, take ripe figs, crush them with pigeon droppings, and similar medicines that reduce the swelling.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And sometimes the swelling is removed by rubbing continuously and for a long time with moist hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And administer movement to the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the twisting has become aged and hardened like stone, and it is necessary to remove it with iron, it must be cut down to the bone with a fine incision knife, carefully, and apply care and attention to the healing.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations.
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation is the removal of a joint from its place, whereby it cannot move, the limb is misshapen, and the patient feels great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation occurs in someone, it must be reset immediately without delay.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For if delayed, the area swells, and perhaps it will then be difficult to reset it in place; therefore, it should not be moved when it is swollen: often this causes spasms and other pains. However, when this happens, bleed the patient, then leave it until the swelling is calmed; then moisten the limb with warm water and oil, and then reset it gently, and treat each limb as treatment requires in its case.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have arranged the chapters on dislocations from head to foot.
des mandibules	Of the jaws.
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	It seldom happens that both jaws are dislocated, and dislocation of both occurs in two ways: either they are slightly moved out of place and somewhat softened; or they are fully dislocated, hanging down toward the chest, and saliva flows from the mouth as he cannot hold it, nor can he close his mouth, and his tongue is entangled with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is minor, it often corrects itself with certain movements.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And if it is fully and completely dislocated, it must be reset quickly without delay; and in such a way that the assistant holds the patient’s head, and the doctor places his thumb of one hand at the root of the dislocation of the jaw within the mouth, if the dislocation is on both sides; and the other fingers of the hands are outside, to make it level; and instruct the patient to relax his jaws and move them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the doctor aligns it, until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if resetting is difficult, especially if both jaws are involved, moisten them with warm water and oil, until you can reset them gently; and do not delay in the resetting, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they are evenly reset, and the patient’s mouth closes well without relaxing, place cloths moistened with ointment made of rose oil and wax, then bind it lightly with soft ties; let the patient sleep on his back, and his head positioned between two cushions, so that he does not move it to the right or left, and does not strain to chew, but takes soft food, until the pain is gone, and the jaws are healed; then he may eat whatever he likes lightly, without straining to open his mouth for eating and drinking, until the jaw is well set and healed.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if both jaws cannot be reset promptly, and do not return to their places, then fevers and recurring ailments arise, and possibly diarrhea, or possibly vomiting of pure bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	And when you see this, then know that it is fatal; and often those to whom it occurs die within nine days.
de la forcelle	Of the clavicle.
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The clavicle cannot dislocate inward along its continuation with the chest, and sometimes it dislocates outward, and this is easily felt.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And the treatment is that the patient should often lie on his back and stretch his arms; then press firmly on the area with your palm, and it will return; then apply a plaster and a bandage, and secure it tightly; and the end near the shoulder cannot dislocate easily, and if it does dislocate, reset it in place, as we have said; then apply a plaster and bandage, secure it tightly, and instruct the patient to rest until it is healed; and similarly, the shoulder joint is reset when it is out of place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	Of shoulder dislocation.
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	Know that the shoulder only dislocates in three ways: one is that it dislocates below, toward the armpit; the second is toward the chest; and sometimes it dislocates upward, though this is rare; it does not dislocate backward due to the shoulder, nor inward due to the nerves; it often dislocates downward toward the armpit, especially in those who have little flesh, as it easily dislocates in them; in those with ample flesh, it dislocates with difficulty and is equally hard to return to place.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	Sometimes, it happens that certain men experience a blow or fracture, causing the shoulder to swell with a hot abscess, leading them to believe it is dislocated as a result.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	Therefore, you must examine it thoroughly to be certain; only then should you begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	The dislocation is recognized when it is displaced downward toward the armpit, and you should observe a clear difference between the affected shoulder and the healthy one. You will find a hollow at the top of the shoulder, and beneath the armpit, touching the top of the shoulder will feel as if it were a bone. The patient will be unable to bring his hand to his nose or move it in any direction. Also, if the shoulder is dislocated upward, this is not hidden, as you can clearly feel it upon touch. This type of dislocation is not difficult to correct if it is recent or if the patient is a child.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	The method is for the assistant to lift the patient’s arm upward, then place your fingers under the armpit, and forcefully raise the joint back into its place; the assistant lifts the arm, extending it upward, then returns it below. It will realign quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	If the shoulder does not return to its position as we described within a few days, it is necessary for the patient to be bathed in warm water. Let the assistants prepare a softening and soothing treatment, such as a decoction of marshmallow, fenugreek, and melilot in water, and apply it. Then lay the patient on their back, placing an evenly thick woolen cushion beneath the armpit, not too soft and not too hard. The physician should place their heel on the cushion and carefully lift the head of the shoulder, pulling the patient’s arm. Meanwhile, another assistant should hold the patient’s head to prevent it from moving downward; this will cause the shoulder to realign immediately. If you wish, another method involves having a person who is taller than the patient stand to the side of the injured shoulder; they should place their shoulder under the patient’s armpit and lift the armpit upwards, so the patient hangs in the air. Then, another assistant should pull the patient’s arm downward toward the abdomen.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too light, he should be weighed down with something heavy, and the dislocation will return immediately.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment;  et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And one also resets it in another manner: a long stick is driven into the ground, the head shaped round like a pestle, and neither too thick nor too thin; it is then placed under the patient, with a soft cloth over it, and the patient stands along the length of the stick; his hand is stretched downward strongly from the other side, and the joint will return to its place quickly; and if it still does not want to return with all that we have said, then do this remedy: take a stake two arm's length long and four fingers wide, with a rounded head to go deep under the armpit, in this manner:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	then tie soft cloths on the head of the stake, so that it does not hurt the patient; place it under the patient’s armpit; extend his arm along the length of the stake, tie the support on the stake and the arm at the head of the hand, then place the arm over a rung of a wide ladder, and let the hand stretch downward, with the body left hanging on the other side: the joint will go back in immediately.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is in place, in whatever manner it may be, it is necessary to place an equal ball of wool under the armpit, then apply a plaster prepared with mill powder, along with incense and a bit of egg, over the entire shoulder and around it, then gently tighten it under the armpit, wrap the binding over the plaster, and hold the hand to the neck, leaving the hand to remain this way.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And he should eat little, so that the limb is strengthened, for it will heal more quickly; then he can eat more after five or seven days, and move it; and if it is firm and has not softened, it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is out of place due to moisture that has entered it, or for another reason, it is necessary to administer cauterizations in three points, as previously described in the chapter on cauterizations.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this, and it loosens after seven days, and the joint does not hold, and he cannot lift his arm upward, then know that the nerves at the head of the shoulder are cut, stretched, or weakened; and know that the joint will never again be fixed in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation that is toward the chest and the nipples, or behind, is done by pressure and stretching of the hands, and another method is applied there; and treat it until it is healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if, after healing, stiffness comes to the limb, and delay in movement, then let the patient take baths many times, until that stiffness is relieved, and it returns to its former nature.
de la dislocation dou coute	On the dislocation of the elbow
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the elbow joint is dislocated with difficulty, and returns with difficulty; it is dislocated in all directions, especially front and back, and the dislocation is not hard to notice, as it is easily seen and felt; it dislocates according to each position.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the afflicted elbow with the healthy one, you can see it clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is stiff, and he cannot bend the arm, nor touch his shoulder with it.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it is necessary to reset it before a hot abscess forms, for if a hot abscess does come, it will be hard to reset; and perhaps it cannot be fully reset, especially when it is toward the back; it is worse than other dislocations, is more painful, and sometimes causes death.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the resetting is done, when it is such that it can be restored, by extending his hand with your two hands; his arms are spread, and the physician’s hands around the elbow, above and below, push the joint with his thumbs together, or with the root of his palm, until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is toward the front, it returns when he clasps his hand in his hand, and strikes the root of his palm on the dislocated elbow.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And if it does not want to return to its place, then administer a strong extension; this means that two assistants extend the arm and hold it steady so that it does not move during the extension; then turn the arm from side to side, after wrapping it in a cloth that is both long and wide; and when the doctor has brought the joint to his hand, he anoints it with some oil to soften the joint, then presses the joint firmly until it returns to its place; and when it is in place, he applies a dry plaster with some egg white, binds it tightly, suspends the patient’s arm from his neck, leaves it for some days, then unbinds it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firm in its place, untie the bandage, and leave it; and if you see that the joint does not hold well, then repeat the plaster and bandage, and leave it thus for several days, until it is firmly set; then untie it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And if he feels pain after the return of the joint, and it moves, then bathe it and gently rub it, pressing until it is relieved; or place a sheep's fat wool poultice on the joint, leave it for one day and one night, then remove it and have him enter the bath; and when he sweats, gently rub the joint, then put the poultice back on, and then go back into the bath; do this two or three times until he is healed; and if you wish, apply warm, moist cow dung mixed with butter, and bind it over; thus it will return to its normal state.
li dislocation de la main	The dislocation of the hand.
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The joint of the hand is dislocated, and its resetting is easier than for other joints. However, it is necessary to bring it back to place quickly, in the very hour it is dislocated, before the area swells or an inflamed abscess develops.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparence de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	And the resetting is done by placing the injured hand on a table, and the assistant extends the hand, and the doctor aligns it, placing his palm over the prominent part of the joint, pressing until it returns. However, you must ensure it is properly positioned; then the patient places the back of his hand on a table for extension and resetting.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparence de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is on the back of the hand, the patient places the back of his hand on the table, and the doctor places his hand over the prominent part of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If it returns immediately, that is good. If not, apply soothing plasters for inflamed abscesses, and leave it thus without resetting.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	And if he cannot endure it, and you cannot set it back in place after some days, the joint remains twisted; and this only harms the patient to the extent that the hand is weakened and cannot grip anything firmly: in that case, know that the nerves are cut, or the artery; there is no other remedy than cauterization near the affected area, and perhaps nothing else will work.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse V jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is in place, apply the plaster we have described, then bandage it and leave it for five days, then untie it and leave it thus.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he cannot move it well, and there is some stiffness, bathe it in warm water, and rub it until it heals.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	On the dislocation of the fingers of the hand.
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	Sometimes the fingers of the hand are dislocated to each side, sometimes on the back of the palm or the front; then extend the finger, and push the dislocation towards your fingers until it returns, then support the tip of the finger, letting it hang towards the part where it is disjointed; leave it for two days, then straighten it on that day; and bind it at night, as we have said, and unbind it by day, moving it, and rebind it at night; do this frequently until it is firm, and do the same if it is dislocated at the front of the hand, following the instructions above, until it heals; and do the same for dislocation on any other side.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	On the dislocation of the spine of the back.
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the spine of the back or neck is dislocated, or there are multiple dislocations, there is no cure, for death quickly approaches the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	And the signs are that the excretions flow without control, and cannot be held, and often one limb is weakened, or both thighs or both arms; and often the spine is distorted in four directions; that which curves backward is called "humpback": the treatment is to check if the humpback has been there since childhood; if so, there is no cure or healing for it.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	And for that which comes from falling or blows or similar causes, the ancients described treatments in many words, though not all of it is very effective; but I have shortened it according to my understanding, and I have crafted instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	I say that in the hump that appears on the front of the chest, there is neither skill nor health; likewise for the one that appears directly on both sides, and it cannot be cured except the one that appears on the back, as I say; and this requires that the patient be stretched out on his face on an even surface, with padding beneath him so that he is not injured; then drive a stake firmly into the ground at the head and another at the feet, and tie a strap under the patient’s armpits, another at the hips, at the knees, and at the ankles; and two assistants pull the straps, one at the head and the other at the feet, between the two stakes; and the stakes should be very secure, as we have said, and the doctor places his palms firmly on the spine until it returns to its place.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	And if it does not return through this treatment, then take a plank three arm-lengths long, and brace one end against the wall, with the patient lying on his side, and place the middle of the plank on the spine; then the doctor should put his feet on the other end of the plank and press firmly until it returns to its place; and if you wish, do this with a hand-turned winch.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	And this involves placing two stakes at the patient’s head, one arm-length apart, and two more toward the feet, with a palm’s width of space between each stake, above and below; and each stake should have a hole through which the winch can pass, and the stakes should be firmly set in the ground so that they do not move; and between each pair of stakes there should be a rotating stake on which the straps turn, with two small handles on each winch, a palm’s length, to turn the winch; then tie the strap under the armpits to the winch at the head, and the strap near the feet to the other winch, and each assistant turns his winch along with the strap, while the master aligns the spine evenly as we have described.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	And when it is aligned, apply a drying plaster with some egg white, then the padding, and then a splint from a small board three fingers long, covering the area of the hump and the healthy part of the spine, then bind it with a strap as we have described, and the patient should consume light nourishment until he is healed; and if anything appears at the end of the healing, softening and soothing medicines must be applied, along with the splint we mentioned before; and sometimes a piece of lead is applied, and sometimes an appearance shows up on the last vertebra of the spine, and it is thought to be a dislocation; and it is the bone that appears, which should not be presumed, for it could bring death.
des dislocations de la hainche	On the dislocations of the hip.
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties: dedens et defuer, et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	Know that in the joints of the hip and shoulder only dislocations occur, unlike other joints; and the hip joint is dislocated in four directions: inward, outward, forward, and backward; more often inward than elsewhere, and rarely forward or backward.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	The indication of an inward dislocation is that when the injured leg is placed beside the healthy one, it appears longer, and the patient’s knee protrudes more than the healthy one, and the patient cannot bend his knee towards the fire; and the area nearby is swollen from an inflamed abscess, because the head of the thighbone presses there.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	The sign of an outward dislocation is that the symptoms are opposite to those just described.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	The sign of a forward dislocation is that he can extend his leg fully; however, he cannot bend his knee without pain, and if one tries to make him walk, he cannot go forward and retains his urine, and the groin swells, and when he walks, he steps on his heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	The sign of a backward dislocation is that he cannot extend or bend his knee, and that leg is more twisted than the other, the groin is softened, and the head of the thighbone is in the position beneath the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The treatment of this type of dislocation is that you should check if the dislocation is old, and if it has remained as such for a long time, then it has no cure; there should be no presumption otherwise.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	But if the dislocation is recent, and it is one of the four types of dislocations, quickly turn the joint, and extend it inward and outward, and move it to the right and left; perhaps it will return, and no other treatment will be necessary.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And if it does not return in this way, you need to prepare a strong assistant, and stretch the leg firmly with two hands, or with a band tied above the knee; another assistant places his hands under his armpits, then ties a soft band on the thigh; and another holds the end of the band; and they all stretch up and down at once, so that the patient is lifted from the ground, and he remains hanging.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as IIII semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of extension is common to all four types, and if the dislocation returns as we have described, that is good.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If not, apply a treatment according to the type. When the dislocation is inward, the patient should lie on his healthy side, then place a band on the base of the thigh and the area beneath the groin, then stretch the band upwards towards the groin and towards the hip; then let another assistant grasp his arms, embrace the thick part of the injured thigh, and extend it outward strongly: it will return to its place immediately; and this type of dislocation is easier to treat than the others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	And if you cannot secure it in this manner as we have described, then tie the patient’s two feet together with a strong soft band at both heels and knees, and the injured leg should be extended two fingers more than the other; then he should be hung from the top of a pole, two arm’s lengths above the ground; then instruct one assistant to embrace the head of the thigh, and another assistant should hang with the patient, strongly embracing the thigh, for the joint will return quickly.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And when the dislocation is outward, let the patient lie down, as we said for one who has a humpback, and place a band carefully around the injured leg and also at the foot; then place two supports, one at the head and the other at the feet, then place a support between the patient’s thighs, in the middle of the hip area; and wrap moistened cloths around, so that he is not harmed, then each assistant stretches towards himself, and the doctor adjusts the dislocation with his hand.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, that is good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If not, place him on a table, and press as we described for a humpback, with the patient lying on his healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is forward, the injured leg must be extended quickly, as I have said; then the doctor presses his palm on the injured groin, pressing with the other hand and stretching downward towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.
