And if the dislocation is outward, it is not necessary to stretch the patient downwards or lift him up from the ground; rather, he should be positioned as if the hip were dislocated outward, as we have described regarding lying on both hips; he should be on his face, and the strap stretched as we mentioned above, and pressure should be applied to the joint on the table; it will be correctly aligned when the patient extends his legs and they are even; then bring the thighs together, apply the plaster, and bind with a band so that the hip does not move; let him rest for three or four days, then unbind it and reapply the plaster; if you see they are even, bind it again as before and leave it for three days; then unbind it and let him walk gently until the limb is strengthened.
de la dislocation dou genoil	of the dislocation of the knee
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The knee is dislocated in three ways: that is, inward, outward, and backward; and it is not dislocated forward.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And the sign is that you instruct the patient to bend his leg to his thigh, and if it does not press against his thigh, know that it is dislocated; and the restoration of it all is that you make the patient sit upright, and extend his leg if he can, and place your back against his thigh, and place his foot against your feet; then take his knee with your palms, and pull between your fingers, then press firmly on both sides of the knee; and another assistant extends his foot until the knee returns to its place, and the sign is that his leg presses easily against his thigh; then place the plaster on it, and make the leg press to the thigh, and bind them together tightly for three or four days, then unbind it; and the patient should not strain himself by walking until the limb is strengthened.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limb is not in place, then administer a strong extension, as we have said in the treatment of the hip, until it is healed.
de la dislocation dou talon	of the dislocation of the heel
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heel is sometimes displaced, and sometimes fully dislocated, both inward and outward.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the sign is that the ankle is swollen, and stretches forward to the part where it is dislocated: the repositioning is easy, and one should gently extend it with the hands when it is only displaced.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is fully dislocated, it is necessary for you to make the patient sit upright, and have an assistant hold the leg above the ankle; then pull the foot toward you with your right hand, then with the left twice, then stretch it upwards, and gently push the foot upward; and do this twice, as we have said, by pushing and pulling the foot; if it returns, that is good; if not, start the procedure over, for it will return; and if it cannot return like this, make the patient lie on his back on the ground, and firmly place a bar in the ground between his thighs, and wrap cloths around it so it doesn’t harm the patient; then have one assistant hold the thigh, and another assistant extend the foot with his hands or a band tied around the ankle; then each assistant should stretch equally, and the bar should always be between the patient’s thighs to hold him as they stretch; then the doctor carefully sets the dislocation by hand, and another assistant holds the sound leg below, and the dislocation will return quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And when it is in place, put on a plaster and stoppers, and bind it firmly, and tie the foot to the leg, and take care of the nerves behind the ankle so that the bandage is not too tight; then leave it for two or three days, and if the bandage loosens, tighten it; then untie it on the third or fourth day, and prohibit the patient from walking for four days; and if he walks before that time, there is no assurance that it will not dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if a hot swelling appears, it is necessary that you soothe it, as we have said elsewhere, until it is healed.
des dois	of the fingers
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the fingers are dislocated, it is necessary to gently extend them without exertion, and it is an easy matter.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation is in some joint on the back of the foot, then it is necessary for you to make the patient sit on a flat place or on a table straight, and place your foot on the visible joint, then press firmly with your foot until it returns; and when it is even, and nothing is visible, place under the sole of the foot a board with two supports, then bind it firmly, and leave it for three days, then untie it; and let it rest until it is healed.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of a wound and dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When a wound comes with the dislocation, and one wishes to restore it, it often happens that the patient dies: so do not be presumptuous in the treatment, if you are not wise in the art and have not long practiced it, and if you are not compassionate, merciful, and cautious, not bold; and use from the beginning things that soothe hot swelling, and leave the patient in God’s hands if you do not see hope of healing; and when you see hope, then immediately return the limb to its place, before the hot swelling appears there; and when the limb is in place, administer things to soothe hot swelling, and treat the wound, as needed, with drying ointments; and if with the dislocation there is a fracture, and small bones are separated, then remove them, and do as we have said for simple injuries; and beware of proceeding in fear, as I have said, for this will earn you rewards from your Creator, and for the safety of your soul and your body.
Amen	Amen
